     <p>
      The
      <b>
       history of Israel
      </b>
      encompasses the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Land_of_Israel" title="History of the Jews in the Land of Israel">
       history of the Jews in the Land of Israel
      </a>
      , as well as the history of the modern
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">
       State of Israel
      </a>
      . The area of modern Israel is small, about the size of
      <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">
       Wales
      </a>
      or half the size of
      <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
       Costa Rica
      </a>
      , and is located roughly on the site of the
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">
       ancient kingdoms of Israel and Judah
      </a>
      except that these ancient kingdoms also included what is now the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      . It is the birthplace of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
       Hebrew language
      </a>
      spoken in Israel, and of the
      <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">
       Abrahamic religions
      </a>
      . It contains sites sacred to
      <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
       Judaism
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">
       Druze
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah' Faith">
       Bah' Faith
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Although coming under the sway of various empires and home to a variety of ethnicities, the
      <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">
       Land of Israel
      </a>
      was predominantly
      <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
       Jewish
      </a>
      until the 3rd century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The area became increasingly
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christian
      </a>
      after the 3rd century and then largely
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
       Muslim
      </a>
      some centuries following the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Syria" title="Muslim conquest of Syria">
       7th century conquest
      </a>
      until the middle of the 20th century. It was a focal point of conflict between Christianity and Islam between 1096 and 1291, and from the end of the
      <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
       Crusades
      </a>
      until the
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_and_Palestine_Campaign" title="Sinai and Palestine Campaign">
       British conquest in 1917
      </a>
      was part of the Syrian province of first the
      <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">
       Mamluk Sultanate of Egypt
      </a>
      and then (from 1517) the
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman Empire
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In the late-19th century, persecution of Jews, particularly in Europe, led to the creation of the Zionist movement. Following the British conquest of Syria, the
      <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration" title="Balfour Declaration">
       Balfour Declaration
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
       World War I
      </a>
      and the formation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">
       Mandate of Palestine
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">
       Aliyah
      </a>
      (Jewish immigration to the
      <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">
       Land of Israel
      </a>
      ) increased and gave rise to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zionist_and_Palestinian_Arab_attitudes_before_1948" title="Zionist and Palestinian Arab attitudes before 1948">
       ArabJewish tensions
      </a>
      , and a collision of the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_nationalism" title="Palestinian nationalism">
       Arab
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">
       Jewish
      </a>
      nationalist movements.
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Israeli Declaration of Independence">
       Israeli independence
      </a>
      in 1948 was marked by massive migration of Jews from both
      <a href="/wiki/Bricha" title="Bricha">
       Europe
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries" title="Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries">
       Muslim countries
      </a>
      to Israel, and of
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus" title="1948 Palestinian exodus">
       Arabs
      </a>
      from Israel leading to the extensive
      <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="ArabIsraeli conflict">
       ArabIsraeli conflict
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      About 42% of the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_population_by_country" title="Jewish population by country">
       world's Jews
      </a>
      live in Israel today, the largest Jewish community in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Since about 1970, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      has become the principal
      <a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="IsraelUnited States relations">
       ally of Israel
      </a>
      . In 1979 an uneasy
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_Peace_Treaty" title="EgyptIsrael Peace Treaty">
       EgyptIsrael Peace Treaty
      </a>
      was signed, based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Camp_David_Accords" title="Camp David Accords">
       Camp David Accords
      </a>
      . In 1993 Israel signed
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo_I_Accord" title="Oslo I Accord">
       Oslo I Accord
      </a>
      with the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">
       Palestine Liberation Organization
      </a>
      and in 1994
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_Treaty_of_Peace" title="IsraelJordan Treaty of Peace">
       IsraelJordan Treaty of Peace
      </a>
      was signed. Despite
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_process_in_the_Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Peace process in the IsraeliPalestinian conflict">
       efforts to establish peace between Israel and Palestinians
      </a>
      , many of whom live in Israel or in
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">
       Israeli-occupied territories
      </a>
      , the conflict continues to play a major role in Israeli and international political, social and economic life.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Israel" title="Economy of Israel">
       economy of Israel
      </a>
      was initially primarily socialist and the country dominated by social democratic parties until the 1970s. Since then the Israeli economy has gradually moved to capitalism and a free market economy, partially retaining the social welfare system.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
       Prehistory
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_the_Levant" title="Prehistory of the Levant">
       Prehistory of the Levant
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Between 2.6 and 0.9 million years ago, at least four episodes of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hominine" title="Hominine">
       hominine
      </a>
      dispersal from Africa to the Levant are known, each culturally distinct. The flint tool artifacts of these early humans have been discovered on the territory of the current state of Israel, including, at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiron" title="Yiron">
       Yiron
      </a>
      , the oldest stone tools found anywhere outside Africa. Other groups include 1.4 million years old
      <a href="/wiki/Acheulean" title="Acheulean">
       Acheulean
      </a>
      industry, the Bizat Ruhama group and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gesher_Bnot_Yaakov" title="Gesher Bnot Yaakov">
       Gesher Bnot Yaakov
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the Carmel mountain range at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tabun,_Israel" title="Tabun, Israel">
       el-Tabun
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Es_Skhul" title="Es Skhul">
       Es Skhul
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">
       Neanderthal
      </a>
      and early modern human remains were found, including the skeleton of a Neanderthal female, named Tabun I, which is regarded as one of the most important human fossils ever found.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The excavation at el-Tabun produced the longest
      <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy" title="Stratigraphy">
       stratigraphic record
      </a>
      in the region, spanning 600,000 or more years of human activity,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">
       Lower Paleolithic
      </a>
      to the present day, representing roughly a million years of
      <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">
       human evolution
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_times">
       Ancient times
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ancient times">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">
       History of ancient Israel and Judah
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Egyptian_rule">
       Egyptian rule
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Egyptian rule">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:14_century_BC_Eastern.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="578" data-file-width="1041" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/14_century_BC_Eastern.png/350px-14_century_BC_Eastern.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/14_century_BC_Eastern.png/525px-14_century_BC_Eastern.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/14_century_BC_Eastern.png/700px-14_century_BC_Eastern.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:14_century_BC_Eastern.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of the
        <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">
         Ancient Near East
        </a>
        during the
        <a href="/wiki/Amarna_Period" title="Amarna Period">
         Amarna Period
        </a>
        , showing the great powers of the day: Egypt (orange),
        <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">
         Hatti
        </a>
        (blue), the
        <a href="/wiki/Kassites" title="Kassites">
         Kassite
        </a>
        kingdom of Babylon (black),
        <a href="/wiki/Middle_Assyrian_Empire" title="Middle Assyrian Empire">
         Middle Assyrian Empire
        </a>
        (yellow), and Mitanni (brown). The extent of the Achaean/Mycenaean civilization is shown in purple.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the 2nd millennium BC,
      <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
       Canaan
      </a>
      , part of which later became known as Israel, was dominated by
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      from c.1550 to c. 1180.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Israelites">
       Early Israelites
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early Israelites">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrews" title="Hebrews">
       Hebrews
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">
       Israelites
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Biblical_judges" title="Biblical judges">
       Biblical judges
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Origins_of_Judaism" title="Origins of Judaism">
       Origins of Judaism
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_artifacts_significant_to_the_Bible" title="List of artifacts significant to the Bible">
       List of artifacts significant to the Bible
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Bible_and_history" title="The Bible and history">
       The Bible and history
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="531" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG/170px-Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG/255px-Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG/340px-Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Merneptah_Israel_Stele_Cairo.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merneptah_stele" title="Merneptah stele">
         Merneptah stele
        </a>
        . While alternative translations exist, the majority of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblical_Archeology" title="Biblical Archeology">
         biblical archeologists
        </a>
        translate a set of hieroglyphs as "Israel", representing the first instance of the name Israel in the historical record.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first record of the name Israel (as
      <i>
       <span lang="egy-Latn">
        ysrr
       </span>
      </i>
      ) occurs in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merneptah_stele" title="Merneptah stele">
       Merneptah stele
      </a>
      , erected for Egyptian Pharaoh
      <a href="/wiki/Merneptah" title="Merneptah">
       Merneptah
      </a>
      c. 1209 BCE, "Israel is laid waste and his seed is not."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/William_G._Dever" title="William G. Dever">
       William Dever
      </a>
      sees this "Israel" in the central highlands as a cultural and probably political entity, more an ethnic group rather than an organized state.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Ancestors of the Israelites may have included
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semites" title="Semites">
       Semites
      </a>
      native to
      <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">
       Canaan
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Sea_Peoples" title="Sea Peoples">
       Sea Peoples
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      McNutt says, "It is probably safe to assume that sometime during
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
       Iron Age
      </a>
      I a population began to identify itself as 'Israelite'", differentiating itself from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canaanites" title="Canaanites">
       Canaanites
      </a>
      through such markers as the prohibition of intermarriage, an emphasis on family history and genealogy, and religion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first use of
      <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">
       grapheme
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Proto-Sinaitic_script" title="Proto-Sinaitic script">
       writing originated in the area
      </a>
      , probably among Canaanite peoples resident in Egypt. All modern
      <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">
       alphabetical writing systems
      </a>
      are descended from this writing.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Written evidence of the use of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Hebrew" title="Classical Hebrew">
       Classical Hebrew
      </a>
      exists from about 1000 BCE. It was written using the
      <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Hebrew_alphabet" title="Paleo-Hebrew alphabet">
       Paleo-Hebrew alphabet
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Villages had populations of up to 300 or 400,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcnutt70_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mcnutt70-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which lived by farming and herding, and were largely self-sufficient;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      economic interchange was prevalent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Writing was known and available for recording, even in small sites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The archaeological evidence indicates a society of village-like centres, but with more limited resources and a small population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_and_Judah">
       Israel and Judah
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Israel and Judah">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(united_monarchy)" title="Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)">
       Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Kingdom of Judah
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Judah" title="Kings of Judah">
       Kings of Judah
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="859" data-file-width="720" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg/170px-Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg/255px-Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg/340px-Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kingdoms_of_Israel_and_Judah_map_830.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Kingdoms of
        <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
         Israel
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
         Judah
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">
       Hebrew Bible
      </a>
      describes constant warfare between the Jews and other tribes, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">
       Philistines
      </a>
      , whose capital was
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">
       Gaza
      </a>
      . The Bible states that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_David" title="King David">
       King David
      </a>
      founded a dynasty of kings and that his son
      <a href="/wiki/Solomon" title="Solomon">
       Solomon
      </a>
      built a
      <a href="/wiki/Solomon%27s_Temple" title="Solomon's Temple">
       Temple
      </a>
      . No material evidence indisputably of Solomon's reign has been found.
      <a href="/wiki/Yigael_Yadin" title="Yigael Yadin">
       Yigael Yadin
      </a>
      's excavations at
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Hazor" title="Tel Hazor">
       Hazor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Megiddo" title="Tel Megiddo">
       Megiddo
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beit_Shean" title="Beit Shean">
       Beit Shean
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gezer" title="Gezer">
       Gezer
      </a>
      uncovered structures that he and others have argued date from his reign,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but others, such as Israel Finkelstein and Neil Silberman (who agree that Solomon was a historical king), argue that they should be dated to the
      <a href="/wiki/Omrides" title="Omrides">
       Omride
      </a>
      period, more than a century after Solomon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finkelstein_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Finkelstein-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This building is not mentioned in surviving extra-biblical accounts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Possible references to the "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Davidic_Dynasty" title="Davidic Dynasty">
       House of David
      </a>
      " have been found at two sites, the
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Dan_Stele" title="Tel Dan Stele">
       Tel Dan Stele
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mesha_Stele" title="Mesha Stele">
       Mesha Stele
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both David and Solomon are widely referenced in Jewish, Christian and Islamic texts.
     </p>
     <p>
      Around 930 BCE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(united_monarchy)" title="Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)">
       kingdom
      </a>
      split into a southern
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">
       Kingdom of Judah
      </a>
      and a northern
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">
       Kingdom of Israel
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      It is possible that an alliance between
      <a href="/wiki/Ahab" title="Ahab">
       Ahab
      </a>
      of Israel and Ben Hadad II of
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">
       Damascus
      </a>
      managed to repulse the incursions of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrians" title="Assyrians">
       Assyrians
      </a>
      , with a victory at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Qarqar" title="Battle of Qarqar">
       Battle of Qarqar
      </a>
      (854 BCE). (see the
      <a href="/wiki/Kurkh_Monoliths" title="Kurkh Monoliths">
       Kurkh Monoliths
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the Kingdom of Israel was eventually destroyed by
      <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">
       Assyrian
      </a>
      king
      <a href="/wiki/Tiglath-Pileser_III" title="Tiglath-Pileser III">
       Tiglath-Pileser III
      </a>
      around 750 BCE. The Philistine kingdom was also destroyed. The Assyrians sent most of the northern Israelite kingdom into
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_captivity_of_Israel" title="Assyrian captivity of Israel">
       exile
      </a>
      , thus creating the "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lost_Tribes_of_Israel" title="Lost Tribes of Israel">
       Lost Tribes of Israel
      </a>
      ". The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samaritan" title="Samaritan">
       Samaritans
      </a>
      claim to be descended from survivors of the Assyrian conquest. An Israelite revolt (724722 BCE) was crushed after the siege and capture of
      <a href="/wiki/Samaria" title="Samaria">
       Samaria
      </a>
      by the Assyrian king
      <a href="/wiki/Sargon_II" title="Sargon II">
       Sargon II
      </a>
      . Sargon's son,
      <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib" title="Sennacherib">
       Sennacherib
      </a>
      , tried and failed to
      <a href="/wiki/Sennacherib%27s_campaign_in_Judah" title="Sennacherib's campaign in Judah">
       conquer
      </a>
      Judah.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taylor_prism" title="Taylor prism">
       Assyrian records
      </a>
      say he leveled 46 walled cities and besieged Jerusalem, leaving after receiving extensive tribute.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Modern scholars believe that refugees from the destruction of Israel moved to Judah during the rule of King
      <a href="/wiki/Hezekiah" title="Hezekiah">
       Hezekiah
      </a>
      (ruler from 715 - 686 BCE), greatly expanding Jerusalem and leading to construction of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siloam_Tunnel" title="Siloam Tunnel">
       Siloam Tunnel
      </a>
      which could provide water during a siege.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The refugees brought with them new religious ideas which led, under King
      <a href="/wiki/Josiah" title="Josiah">
       Josiah
      </a>
      (ruler from 641 - 619), to the writing of the books of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deuteronomy" title="Deuteronomy">
       Deuteronomy
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Joshua" title="Book of Joshua">
       Joshua
      </a>
      and to the accounts of the kingship of David and Solomon in the
      <a href="/wiki/Books_of_Kings" title="Books of Kings">
       book of Kings
      </a>
      . The books are known as
      <a href="/wiki/Deuteronomist" title="Deuteronomist">
       Deuteronomist
      </a>
      and considered to be a major key step in the emergence of
      <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">
       Monotheism
      </a>
      in Judah. They were written at a time that Assyria was weakened by the emergence of Babylon and may be a committing to text of more ancient verbal traditions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Exile_under_Babylon_.28586.E2.80.93538_BCE.29">
       Exile under Babylon (586538 BCE)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Exile under Babylon (586538 BCE)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Yehud_(Babylonian_province)" title="Yehud (Babylonian province)">
       Yehud (Babylonian province)
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">
       Babylonian captivity
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 586 BCE King
      <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_II" title="Nebuchadnezzar II">
       Nebuchadnezzar II
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">
       Babylon
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish%E2%80%93Babylonian_war" title="JewishBabylonian war">
       conquered
      </a>
      Judah. According to the Hebrew Bible, he destroyed
      <a href="/wiki/Solomon%27s_Temple" title="Solomon's Temple">
       Solomon's Temple
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">
       exiled
      </a>
      the Jews to Babylon. The defeat was also recorded by the Babylonians
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (see the
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_Chronicles" title="Babylonian Chronicles">
       Babylonian Chronicles
      </a>
      ). Babylonian and Biblical sources suggest that the Judean king,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jehoiachin" title="Jehoiachin">
       Jehoiachin
      </a>
      , switched allegiances between the Egyptians and the Babylonians and that invasion was a punishment for allying with Babylon's principal rival, Egypt. The exiled Jews may have been restricted to the elite.
     </p>
     <p>
      Jehoiachin was eventually released by the Babylonians (see
      <a href="/wiki/Jehoiachin%27s_Rations_Tablets" title="Jehoiachin's Rations Tablets">
       Jehoiachin's Rations Tablets
      </a>
      ) and according to both the Bible and the Talmud, the Judean royal family (the
      <a href="/wiki/Davidic_line" title="Davidic line">
       Davidic line
      </a>
      ) continued as head of the exile in Babylon (the
      <a href="/wiki/Exilarch" title="Exilarch">
       Exilarch
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_era_.28538_BCE.E2.80.93636_CE.29">
       Classical era (538 BCE636 CE)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Classical era (538 BCE636 CE)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Persian_and_Hellenistic_rule_538.E2.80.93160_BCE">
       Persian and Hellenistic rule 538160 BCE
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Persian and Hellenistic rule 538160 BCE">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Yehud_Medinata" title="Yehud Medinata">
       Yehud Medinata
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Return_to_Zion" title="Return to Zion">
       Return to Zion
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Second_Temple.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/220px-Second_Temple.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/330px-Second_Temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/440px-Second_Temple.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Second_Temple.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">
         Second Temple
        </a>
        model (
        <a href="/wiki/Israel_Museum" title="Israel Museum">
         Israel Museum
        </a>
        )
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 538 BCE,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrus_(Bible)" title="Cyrus (Bible)">
       Cyrus the Great
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
       Persia
      </a>
      conquered Babylon and took over its empire. Cyrus issued a proclamation granting subjugated nations (including the people of Judah) religious freedom (for the original text see the
      <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Cylinder" title="Cyrus Cylinder">
       Cyrus Cylinder
      </a>
      ). According to the Hebrew Bible 50,000 Judeans, led by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zerubabel" title="Zerubabel">
       Zerubabel
      </a>
      , returned to Judah and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Temple_of_Jerusalem" title="Second Temple of Jerusalem">
       rebuilt the temple
      </a>
      . A second group of 5,000, led by
      <a href="/wiki/Ezra" title="Ezra">
       Ezra
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nehemiah" title="Nehemiah">
       Nehemiah
      </a>
      , returned to Judah in 456 BCE although non-Jews wrote to Cyrus to try to prevent their return.
     </p>
     <p>
      Scholars believe that the final Hebrew versions of the
      <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">
       Torah
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Books_of_Kings" title="Books of Kings">
       Books of Kings
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Authorship_of_the_Bible" title="Authorship of the Bible">
       date from this period
      </a>
      , that the returning
      <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">
       Israelites
      </a>
      adopted an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aramaic_script" title="Aramaic script">
       Aramaic script
      </a>
      (also known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Ashuri_alphabet" title="Ashuri alphabet">
       Ashuri alphabet
      </a>
      ), which they brought back from Babylon; this is the current Hebrew script. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_Calendar" title="Hebrew Calendar">
       Hebrew Calendar
      </a>
      closely resembles the
      <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_calendar" title="Babylonian calendar">
       Babylonian calendar
      </a>
      and probably dates from this period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 333 BCE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">
       Macedonian
      </a>
      ruler
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
       Alexander the Great
      </a>
      defeated
      <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
       Persia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great#Egypt" title="Alexander the Great">
       conquered
      </a>
      the region. Sometime thereafter, the first translation of the Hebrew Bible, the
      <a href="/wiki/Septuagint" title="Septuagint">
       Septuagint
      </a>
      , was begun in
      <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
       Alexandria
      </a>
      . After Alexander's death, his generals fought over the territory he had conquered. Judah became the frontier between the
      <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">
       Seleucid Empire
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Egypt" title="Ptolemaic Egypt">
       Ptolemaic Egypt
      </a>
      , eventually becoming part of the Seleucid Empire in 198 BCE. In the 2nd century BCE,
      <a href="/wiki/Antiochus_IV_Epiphanes" title="Antiochus IV Epiphanes">
       Antiochus IV Epiphanes
      </a>
      (ruler of the Seleucid Empire) tried to eradicate Judaism in favour of
      <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_religion" title="Hellenistic religion">
       Hellenistic religion
      </a>
      . This provoked the 174135 BCE
      <a href="/wiki/Maccabean_Revolt" title="Maccabean Revolt">
       Maccabean Revolt
      </a>
      led by
      <a href="/wiki/Judas_Maccabeus" title="Judas Maccabeus">
       Judas Maccabeus
      </a>
      (whose victory is celebrated in the Jewish festival of
      <a href="/wiki/Hanukkah" title="Hanukkah">
       Hanukkah
      </a>
      ). The
      <a href="/wiki/Books_of_the_Maccabees" title="Books of the Maccabees">
       Books of the Maccabees
      </a>
      describe the uprising and the end of Greek rule. A Jewish party called the
      <a href="/wiki/Hasideans" title="Hasideans">
       Hasideans
      </a>
      opposed both Hellenism
      <i>
       and
      </i>
      the revolt but eventually gave their support to the Maccabees. Modern interpretations see this period as a civil war between Hellenized and orthodox forms of Judaism.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-simpletoremember_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-simpletoremember-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hasmonean_dynasty_160.E2.80.9337_BCE">
       Hasmonean dynasty 16037 BCE
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hasmonean dynasty 16037 BCE">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Hasmonean_dynasty" title="Hasmonean dynasty">
       Hasmonean dynasty
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasmonean" title="Hasmonean">
       Hasmonean
      </a>
      dynasty of (Jewish)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kohen_Gadol" title="Kohen Gadol">
       priest-kings
      </a>
      ruled
      <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">
       Judea
      </a>
      with the
      <a href="/wiki/Pharisees" title="Pharisees">
       Pharisees
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sadducees" title="Sadducees">
       Sadducees
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Essenes" title="Essenes">
       Essenes
      </a>
      as the principal Jewish social movements. As part of the struggle against
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">
       Hellenistic civilization
      </a>
      , the Pharisee leader
      <a href="/wiki/Simeon_ben_Shetach" title="Simeon ben Shetach">
       Simeon ben Shetach
      </a>
      established the first schools based around
      <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">
       meeting houses
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This led to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rabbinical_Judaism" title="Rabbinical Judaism">
       Rabbinical Judaism
      </a>
      . Justice was administered by the
      <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin" title="Sanhedrin">
       Sanhedrin
      </a>
      , which was a Rabbincal assembly and law court whose leader was known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Nasi" title="Nasi">
       Nasi
      </a>
      . The Nasi's religious authority gradually superseded that of the Temple's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kohen_Gadol" title="Kohen Gadol">
       high priest
      </a>
      (under the Hasmoneans this was the king).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 125 BCE the Hasmonean King
      <a href="/wiki/John_Hyrcanus" title="John Hyrcanus">
       John Hyrcanus
      </a>
      subjugated
      <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">
       Edom
      </a>
      and forcibly converted the population to
      <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
       Judaism
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 64 BCE the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
       Roman
      </a>
      general
      <a href="/wiki/Pompey#Pompey_in_the_East" title="Pompey">
       Pompey
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Mithridatic_War" title="Third Mithridatic War">
       conquered
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
       Syria
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(63_BC)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (63 BC)">
       intervened
      </a>
      in the Hasmonean civil war in Jerusalem. In 47 BCE the lives of
      <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">
       Julius Caesar
      </a>
      and his protege
      <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">
       Cleopatra
      </a>
      were saved by 3,000 crack Jewish troops sent by King
      <a href="/wiki/Hyrcanus_II" title="Hyrcanus II">
       Hyrcanus II
      </a>
      and commanded by
      <a href="/wiki/Antipater_the_Idumaean" title="Antipater the Idumaean">
       Antipater
      </a>
      , whose descendants Caesar made kings of Judea.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Herodian_kingdom_37_BCE.E2.80.936_CE">
       Herodian kingdom 37 BCE6 CE
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Herodian kingdom 37 BCE6 CE">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Herodian_kingdom" title="Herodian kingdom">
       Herodian kingdom
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tetrarchy_(Judea)" title="Tetrarchy (Judea)">
       Tetrarchy (Judea)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      From 37 BCE to 6 CE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Herodian_dynasty" title="Herodian dynasty">
       Herodian dynasty
      </a>
      , Jewish-Roman client kings, descended from Antipater, ruled Judea.
      <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">
       Herod the Great
      </a>
      considerably enlarged the temple (see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herod%27s_Temple" title="Herod's Temple">
       Herod's Temple
      </a>
      ), making it one of the largest religious structures in the world. Despite its fame, it was in this period that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rabbinical_Judaism" title="Rabbinical Judaism">
       Rabbinical Judaism
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Hillel_the_Elder" title="Hillel the Elder">
       Hillel the Elder
      </a>
      , began to assume popular prominence over the
      <a href="/wiki/Kohen" title="Kohen">
       Temple priesthood
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">
       Jewish Temple
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      was granted special permission not to display an effigy of the emperor, becoming the only religious structure in the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
       Roman Empire
      </a>
      that did not do so. Special dispensation was granted for Jewish citizens of the Roman Empire to pay a
      <a href="/wiki/Fiscus_Judaicus" title="Fiscus Judaicus">
       tax to the temple
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_rule_6.E2.80.93390">
       Roman rule 6390
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Roman rule 6390">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Judea_(Roman_province)" title="Judea (Roman province)">
       Judea (Roman province)
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">
       Syria Palaestina
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_wars" title="JewishRoman wars">
       JewishRoman wars
      </a>
     </div>
     <table class="infobox" style="clear:left">

        </b>

      </tr>

     </table>
     <p>
      Judea was made a Roman province in 6 CE. Following the next decades, though prosperous, the society suffered increasing tensions between Greco-Roman and Judean populations.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 64 CE, the High Priest
      <a href="/wiki/Joshua_ben_Gamla" title="Joshua ben Gamla">
       Joshua ben Gamla
      </a>
      introduced a religious requirement for Jewish boys to learn to read from the age of 6. Over the next few hundred years this requirement became steadily more ingrained in Jewish traditions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 66 CE, the Jews of Judea rose in
      <a href="/wiki/First_Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_War" title="First JewishRoman War">
       revolt
      </a>
      against Rome, naming their new state as "Israel".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The events were described by the Jewish leader/historian
      <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">
       Josephus
      </a>
      , including the desperate defense of
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yodfat" title="Siege of Yodfat">
       Jotapata
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(70)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (70)">
       siege of Jerusalem
      </a>
      (6970 CE) and the desperate last stand at
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Masada" title="Siege of Masada">
       Masada
      </a>
      under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleazar_ben_Yair" title="Eleazar ben Yair">
       Eleazar ben Yair
      </a>
      (7273 CE). Josephus estimated that over a million people died in the siege of Jerusalem. Jerusalem and the Temple lay in ruins. During the Jewish revolt, most
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity" title="History of Christianity">
       Christians
      </a>
      , at this time a sub-sect of Judaism, removed themselves from Judea. The rabbinical/
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharisee" title="Pharisee">
       Pharisee
      </a>
      movement led by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yochanan_ben_Zakai" title="Yochanan ben Zakai">
       Yochanan ben Zakai
      </a>
      , who opposed the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sadducee" title="Sadducee">
       Sadducee
      </a>
      temple priesthood, made peace with Rome and survived. After the war
      <a href="/wiki/Taxation_of_the_Jews" title="Taxation of the Jews">
       Jews continued to be taxed
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Fiscus_Judaicus" title="Fiscus Judaicus">
       Fiscus Judaicus
      </a>
      , which was used to fund a temple to Jupiter.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_3982_nevoraya_synagogue.jpg">
