       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_3982_nevoraya_synagogue.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Nabratein_synagogue" title="Nabratein synagogue">
         Nabratein synagogue
        </a>
        remains in the upper
        <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
         Galilee
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From 115 to 117, Jews in Libya, Egypt, Cyprus, Mesopotamia and
      <a href="/wiki/Lod" title="Lod">
       Lod
      </a>
      rose in
      <a href="/wiki/Kitos_War" title="Kitos War">
       revolt against Rome
      </a>
      . This conflict was accompanied by large-scale massacres of both Romans and Jews. Cyprus was severely depopulated and Jews banned from living there.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 131, the Emperor
      <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">
       Hadrian
      </a>
      renamed Jerusalem "
      <a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">
       Aelia Capitolina
      </a>
      " and constructed a Temple of Jupiter on the site of the former Jewish temple. Jews were banned from living in Jerusalem itself (a ban that persisted until the Arab conquest), and the Roman province, until then known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iudaea_Province" title="Iudaea Province">
       Iudaea Province
      </a>
      , was renamed
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">
       Palaestina
      </a>
      , no other revolt led to a province being renamed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The names "Palestine" (in English) and "Filistin" (in Arabic) are derived from this. From 132 to 136, the Jewish leader
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simon_Bar_Kokhba" title="Simon Bar Kokhba">
       Simon Bar Kokhba
      </a>
      led another major
      <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_revolt" title="Bar Kokhba revolt">
       revolt
      </a>
      against the Romans, again renaming the country "Israel"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (see
      <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kochba_Revolt_coinage" title="Bar Kochba Revolt coinage">
       Bar Kochba Revolt coinage
      </a>
      ). The Bar-Kochba revolt probably caused more trouble for the Romans than the more famous (and better documented) revolt of 70.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Christians refused to participate in the revolt and from this point the Jews regarded Christianity as a separate religion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The revolt was eventually crushed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Hadrian" title="Emperor Hadrian">
       Emperor Hadrian
      </a>
      himself. Although uncertain, it is widely thought that during the Bar Kokhba revolt, when a
      <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Jamnia" title="Council of Jamnia">
       rabbinical assembly decided
      </a>
      which
      <a href="/wiki/Development_of_the_Hebrew_Bible_canon" title="Development of the Hebrew Bible canon">
       books could be regarded
      </a>
      as part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">
       Hebrew Bible
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_apocrypha" title="Jewish apocrypha">
       Jewish apocrypha
      </a>
      were left out.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A rabbi of this period,
      <a href="/wiki/Simeon_bar_Yochai" title="Simeon bar Yochai">
       Simeon bar Yochai
      </a>
      , is regarded as the author of the
      <a href="/wiki/Zohar" title="Zohar">
       Zohar
      </a>
      , the foundational text for Kabbalistic thought. However, modern scholars believe it was written in Medieval Spain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After suppressing the Bar Kochba revolt, the Romans
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_diaspora" title="Jewish diaspora">
       exiled
      </a>
      the Jews of Judea, but not of Galilee and permitted a hereditary Rabbinical Patriarch (from the
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hillel" title="House of Hillel">
       House of Hillel
      </a>
      , based in Galilee) to represent the Jews in dealings with the Romans. The most famous of these was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judah_haNasi" title="Judah haNasi">
       Judah haNasi
      </a>
      who is credited with compiling the final version of the
      <a href="/wiki/Mishnah" title="Mishnah">
       Mishnah
      </a>
      (a massive body of Jewish religious texts interpreting the Bible) and with strengthening the educational demands of Judaism by requiring that illiterate Jews be treated as outcasts. As a result many illiterate Jews may have converted to Christianity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Jewish seminaries, such as those at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shefaram" title="Shefaram">
       Shefaram
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bet_Shearim" title="Bet Shearim">
       Bet Shearim
      </a>
      continued to produce scholars and the best of these became members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sanhedrin" title="Sanhedrin">
       Sanhedrin
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which was located first at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tzippori" title="Tzippori">
       Tzippori
      </a>
      and later at
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Before the Bar-Kochba uprising, an estimated 2/3 of the population of Gallilee and 1/3 of the coastal region were Jewish.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the Galillee, many Synagogues have been found dating from this period. However, persecution and the economic crisis that affected the Roman empire in the 3rd century led to further Jewish migration from
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">
       Syria Palaestina
      </a>
      to the more tolerant Persian
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" title="Sassanid Empire">
       Sassanid Empire
      </a>
      , where a prosperous Jewish community with
      <a href="/wiki/Talmudic_Academies_in_Babylonia" title="Talmudic Academies in Babylonia">
       extensive seminaries
      </a>
      existed in the area of Babylon.
     </p>
     <p>
      Early in the 4th century,
      <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
       Constantinople
      </a>
      became the capital of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Roman_Empire" title="East Roman Empire">
       East Roman Empire
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
       Christianity
      </a>
      was adopted as the official religion. The name Jerusalem was restored to Aelia Capitolina and it became a Christian city. Jews were still banned from living in Jerusalem, but were allowed to visit, and it is in this period that the surviving
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">
       Western Wall
      </a>
      of the temple became sacred. In 3512, another
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_revolt_against_Gallus" title="Jewish revolt against Gallus">
       Jewish revolt
      </a>
      in the Galilee erupted against a corrupt Roman governor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 362, the last
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan" title="Pagan">
       pagan
      </a>
      Roman Emperor,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">
       Julian the Apostate
      </a>
      , announced plans to rebuild the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_in_Jerusalem" title="Temple in Jerusalem">
       Jewish Temple
      </a>
      . He died while fighting the Persians in 363 and the project was discontinued.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Byzantine_rule_390.E2.80.93611">
       Byzantine rule 390611
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Byzantine rule 390611">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">
       Palaestina Prima
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Secunda" title="Palaestina Secunda">
       Palaestina Secunda
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_revolt_against_Heraclius" title="Jewish revolt against Heraclius">
       Jewish revolt against Heraclius
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Rabbinic_literature" title="Rabbinic literature">
       Rabbinic literature
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Roman Empire split in 390 CE and the region became part of the (Christian) East Roman Empire, known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
       Byzantine Empire
      </a>
      . Byzantine Christianity was dominated by the (Greek)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">
       Orthodox Church
      </a>
      . In the 5th century, the
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">
       Western Roman Empire
      </a>
      collapsed leading to Christian migration into the Roman province of
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">
       Palaestina Prima
      </a>
      and development of a Christian majority. Jews numbered 1015% of the population, concentrated largely in the Galilee. Judaism was the only non-Christian religion tolerated, but there were bans on Jews building new places of worship, holding public office or owning slaves. Several
      <a href="/wiki/Samaritan_Revolts" title="Samaritan Revolts">
       Samaritan Revolts
      </a>
      erupted in this period,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      resulting in the decrease of Samaritan community from about a million to a near extinction. Sacred Jewish texts written in Palestine at this time are the
      <a href="/wiki/Gemara" title="Gemara">
       Gemara
      </a>
      (400), the
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Talmud" title="Jerusalem Talmud">
       Jerusalem Talmud
      </a>
      (500) and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passover_Haggadah" title="Passover Haggadah">
       Passover Haggadah
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 611,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persia" title="Sassanid Persia">
       Sassanid Persia
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_War_of_602%E2%80%93628" title="ByzantineSasanian War of 602628">
       invaded
      </a>
      the Byzantine Empire and, after a long siege,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khosrau_II" title="Khosrau II">
       Khosrau II
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(614)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (614)">
       captured Jerusalem
      </a>
      in 614, with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolt_against_Heraclius" title="Revolt against Heraclius">
       Jewish help
      </a>
      , including possibly the Jewish
      <a href="/wiki/Himyarite_Kingdom" title="Himyarite Kingdom">
       Himyarite Kingdom
      </a>
      in Yemen. Jews were left to govern Jerusalem when the Persians took over. The Byzantine Emperor,
      <a href="/wiki/Heraclius" title="Heraclius">
       Heraclius
      </a>
      , promised to restore Jewish rights and received Jewish help in defeating the Persians, but he soon reneged on the agreement after reconquering Palaestina Prima, issuing an edict banning Judaism from the Byzantine Empire. (Egyptian)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coptic_Christians" title="Coptic Christians">
       Coptic Christians
      </a>
      took responsibility for this broken pledge and fasted in penance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_.28636.E2.80.931517.29">
       Middle Ages (6361517)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Middle Ages (6361517)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Jerusalem_(Middle_Ages)" title="History of Jerusalem (Middle Ages)">
       History of Jerusalem (Middle Ages)
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_rule_636.E2.80.931099">
       Arab rule 6361099
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Arab rule 6361099">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Jund Filastin
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn" title="Jund al-Urdunn">
       Jund al-Urdunn
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to Muslim tradition, in 620 Muhammed
      <a href="/wiki/Isra_and_Mi%27raj" title="Isra and Mi'raj">
       was taken on spiritual journey from Mecca
      </a>
      to the "farthest mosque", whose location many consider to be the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mount" title="Temple Mount">
       Temple Mount
      </a>
      , returning the same night. In 634636 the Arabs
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">
       conquered
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">
       Palaestina Prima
      </a>
      and renamed it
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Jund Filastin
      </a>
      , ending the Byzantine ban on Jews living in Jerusalem. Over the next few centuries,
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      replaced Christianity as the dominant religion of the region.
     </p>
     <p>
      From 636 until the beginning of the Crusades,
      <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">
       Jund Filastin
      </a>
      was ruled first by
      <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">
       Medinah
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Rashidun" title="Rashidun">
       Rashidun Caliphs
      </a>
      , then by the
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">
       Damascus
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
       Umayyad Caliphate
      </a>
      and after that the
      <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
       Baghdad
      </a>
      -based
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphs" title="Abbasid Caliphs">
       Abbasid Caliphs
      </a>
      . In 691, Umayyad Caliph
      <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Malik_ibn_Marwan" title="Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan">
       Abd al-Malik
      </a>
      (685705) constructed the
      <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">
       Dome of the Rock
      </a>
      shrine on the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mount" title="Temple Mount">
       Temple Mount
      </a>
      . Jews consider it to contain the
      <a href="/wiki/Foundation_Stone" title="Foundation Stone">
       Foundation Stone
      </a>
      (see also
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kodesh_Hakodashim" title="Kodesh Hakodashim">
       Holy of Holies
      </a>
      ), which is the holiest site in Judaism. A second building, the
      <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Mosque" title="Al-Aqsa Mosque">
       Al-Aqsa Mosque
      </a>
      , was also erected on the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mount" title="Temple Mount">
       Temple Mount
      </a>
      in 705.
     </p>
     <p>
      Between the 7th and 11th centuries, Jewish scribes, called the
      <a href="/wiki/Masoretes" title="Masoretes">
       Masoretes
      </a>
      and located in Galilee and Jerusalem, established the
      <a href="/wiki/Masoretic_Text" title="Masoretic Text">
       Masoretic Text
      </a>
      , the final text of the
      <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">
       Hebrew Bible
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crusader_and_Ayyubid_rule_1099.E2.80.931291">
       Crusader and Ayyubid rule 10991291
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Crusader and Ayyubid rule 10991291">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">
       Kingdom of Jerusalem
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1099jerusalem.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="373" data-file-width="390" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/1099jerusalem.jpg/220px-1099jerusalem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/1099jerusalem.jpg/330px-1099jerusalem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5c/1099jerusalem.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1099jerusalem.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(1099)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (1099)">
         Siege of Jerusalem
        </a>
        , 1099, during the
        <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">
         First Crusade
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1099, the
      <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
       first crusade
      </a>
      took Jerusalem and established a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
       Catholic
      </a>
      kingdom, known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">
       Kingdom of Jerusalem
      </a>
      . During the conquest, both Muslims and Jews were indiscriminately massacred or sold into slavery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pogroms_of_1096" title="Pogroms of 1096">
       murder of Jews
      </a>
      began as the Crusaders traveled across Europe and continued when they reached the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">
       Holy Land
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ashkenazi orthodox Jews still recite a
      <a href="/wiki/Av_HaRachamim" title="Av HaRachamim">
       prayer in memory
      </a>
      of the death and destruction caused by the Crusades.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1187, the
      <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty" title="Ayyubid dynasty">
       Ayyubid
      </a>
      Sultan
      <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">
       Saladin
      </a>
      defeated the Crusaders in the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hattin" title="Battle of Hattin">
       Battle of Hattin
      </a>
      (above
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      ), taking Jerusalem and most of the former Kingdom of Jerusalem. Saladin's court physician was
      <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">
       Maimonides
      </a>
      , whose work had an enormous influence on Judaism. Maimonides was
      <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_Maimonides" title="Tomb of Maimonides">
       buried in Tiberias
      </a>
      . A Crusader state centred round
      <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">
       Acre
      </a>
      survived in weakened form for another century.
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1260 to 1291 the area became the
      <a href="/wiki/Mongol_raids_into_Palestine" title="Mongol raids into Palestine">
       frontier between Mongol invaders
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Franco-Mongol_alliance" title="Franco-Mongol alliance">
       occasional Crusader allies
      </a>
      ) and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">
       Mamluks
      </a>
      of Egypt. The conflict impoverished the country and severely reduced the population. Sultan
      <a href="/wiki/Qutuz" title="Qutuz">
       Qutuz
      </a>
      of Egypt eventually defeated the Mongols in the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">
       Battle of Ain Jalut
      </a>
      (near
      <a href="/wiki/Ein_Harod" title="Ein Harod">
       Ein Harod
      </a>
      ), and his successor (and assassin),
      <a href="/wiki/Baibars" title="Baibars">
       Baibars
      </a>
      , eliminated the last Crusader
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem#The_Kingdom_of_Acre" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">
       Kingdom of Acre
      </a>
      in 1291, thereby ending the Crusades.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mamluk_rule_1260.E2.80.931517">
       Mamluk rule 12601517
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mamluk rule 12601517">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">
       Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Egyptian Mamluk Sultan,
      <a href="/wiki/Baibars" title="Baibars">
       Baibars
      </a>
      (12601277), conquered the region and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">
       Mamluks
      </a>
      ruled it until 1517, regarding it as part of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilad_a-Sham" title="Bilad a-Sham">
       Syria
      </a>
      . In
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      , Baibars banned Jews from worshiping at the
      <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs" title="Cave of the Patriarchs">
       Cave of the Patriarchs
      </a>
      (the second holiest site in Judaism); the ban remained in place until its conquest by Israel 700 years later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The collapse of the Crusades was followed by increased persecution and expulsions of Jews in Europe. Expulsions
      <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Expulsion" title="Edict of Expulsion">
       began in England
      </a>
      (1290) and were followed by France (1306).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Spain,
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Spain#Turning_point_.281212.E2.80.931300.29" title="History of the Jews in Spain">
       persecution
      </a>
      of the highly integrated and successful Jewish community began, including massacres and forced conversions. During the
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">
       Black Death
      </a>
      , many Jews were murdered after being accused of poisoning wells. The completion of the
      <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
       Christian reconquest
      </a>
      of Spain led to expulsion of the Jews of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alhambra_decree" title="Alhambra decree">
       Spain in 1492
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Portugal" title="History of the Jews in Portugal">
       Portugal in 1497
      </a>
      . These were the wealthiest and most integrated Jewish communities in Europe. Many Jews converted to Christianity, however many
      <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">
       secretly practised Judaism
      </a>
      and prejudice against converts (regardless of their sincerity) persisted, leading many former Jews to move to the New World (see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latin_America" title="History of the Jews in Latin America">
       History of the Jews in Latin America
      </a>
      ). Most of the expelled
      <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
       Spanish Jews
      </a>
      moved to North Africa,
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">
       Poland
      </a>
      , to the Ottoman Empire and to the region of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilad_a-Sham" title="Bilad a-Sham">
       Bilad a-Sham
      </a>
      , which roughly corresponds to the ancient
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(united_monarchy)" title="Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)">
       Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)
      </a>
      . In Italy, Jews living in the Papal States were required to live in
      <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">
       ghettos
      </a>
      (see
      <a href="/wiki/Cum_nimis_absurdum" title="Cum nimis absurdum">
       Cum nimis absurdum
      </a>
      ). The last compulsory Ghetto,
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Ghetto" title="Roman Ghetto">
       in Rome
      </a>
      , was abolished in the 1880s.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule_.281517.E2.80.931920.29">
       Ottoman rule (15171920)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ottoman rule (15171920)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Under the Mamluks, the area was a province of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilad_a-Sham" title="Bilad a-Sham">
       Bilad a-Sham
      </a>
      (Syria). It was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Mamluk_War_(1516%E2%80%931517)" title="OttomanMamluk War (15161517)">
       conquered
      </a>
      by Turkish Sultan
      <a href="/wiki/Selim_I" title="Selim I">
       Selim I
      </a>
      in 151617, becoming a part of the province of
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Syria" title="Ottoman Syria">
       Ottoman Syria
      </a>
      for the next four centuries, first as the
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus_Eyalet" title="Damascus Eyalet">
       Damascus Eyalet
      </a>
      and later as the
      <a href="/wiki/Syria_Vilayet" title="Syria Vilayet">
       Syria Vilayet
      </a>
      (following the
      <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">
       Tanzimat
      </a>
      reorganization of 1864).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Yishuv">
       Old Yishuv
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Old Yishuv">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Yishuv" title="Old Yishuv">
       Old Yishuv
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus_Eyalet" title="Damascus Eyalet">
       Damascus Eyalet
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rabbi-Caro.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="308" data-file-width="262" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rabbi-Caro.jpg/170px-Rabbi-Caro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Rabbi-Caro.jpg/255px-Rabbi-Caro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Rabbi-Caro.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rabbi-Caro.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        16th-century
        <a href="/wiki/Safed" title="Safed">
         Safed
        </a>
        rabbi
        <a href="/wiki/Joseph_ben_Ephraim_Karo" title="Joseph ben Ephraim Karo">
         Joseph Karo
        </a>
        , author of the
        <a href="/wiki/Shulchan_Aruch" title="Shulchan Aruch">
         Jewish law book
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From the Middle Ages on, there was small scale individual Jewish migration to the
      <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">
       Land of Israel
      </a>
      , which tended to increase when persecution was bad elsewhere. The Jewish population was concentrated in
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Safed" title="Safed">
       Safed
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      , known in Jewish tradition as the
      <a href="/wiki/Four_Holy_Cities" title="Four Holy Cities">
       Four Holy Cities
      </a>
      . In the 16th century, following a wave of Spanish immigration, Safed became a centre for study of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kabbalah" title="Kabbalah">
       Kabbalah
      </a>
      . However economic decline and conflict between the Druze and the Ottomans, led to the community's gradual decline by the mid-17th century. In 1660, a Druze
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Druze_power_struggle_(1658%E2%80%931667)#Lebanon_and_Galilee_campaign" title="Druze power struggle (16581667)">
       revolt
      </a>
      led to the destruction of the major
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Yishuv" title="Old Yishuv">
       Old Yishuv
      </a>
      cities of
      <a href="/wiki/1660_destruction_of_Safed" title="1660 destruction of Safed">
       Safed
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/1660_destruction_of_Tiberias" title="1660 destruction of Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnay.2C_Y_1992_p._149_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barnay.2C_Y_1992_p._149-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnay.2C_Y_1992_p._149_57-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barnay.2C_Y_1992_p._149-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joel_Rappel_1980_p.531_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Joel_Rappel_1980_p.531-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1663
      <a href="/wiki/Sabbatai_Zevi" title="Sabbatai Zevi">
       Sabbatai Zevi
      </a>
      settled in Jerusalem, proclaiming himself to be the Jewish Messiah. He acquired a large number of followers before going to Istanbul in 1666, where the Sultan forced him to covert to Islam. In the late 18th century a local Bedouin Sheikh
      <a href="/wiki/Daher_el-Omar" title="Daher el-Omar">
       Daher el-Omar
      </a>
      created a de facto independent Emirate in the Galilee. Ottoman attempts to subdue the Sheikh failed, but after Daher's death the Ottomans restored their rule in the area.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1799
      <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">
       Napoleon
      </a>
      briefly
      <a href="/wiki/French_campaign_in_Egypt_and_Syria" title="French campaign in Egypt and Syria">
       occupied
      </a>
      the country and
      <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_and_the_Jews#Bonaparte.27s_proclamation_to_the_Jews_of_Africa_and_Asia" title="Napoleon and the Jews">
       planned a proclamation
      </a>
      inviting Jews to create a state. The proclamation was shelved following his
      <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Acre_(1799)" title="Siege of Acre (1799)">
       defeat at Acre
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1831,
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">
       Muhammad Ali of Egypt
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_(1831%E2%80%931833)" title="EgyptianOttoman War (18311833)">
       conquered
      </a>
      Ottoman Syria and decided to revive and resettle much of its regions. His conscription policies led to a popular
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1834_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="1834 Arab revolt in Palestine">
       Arab revolt
      </a>
      in 1834, resulting in major casualties for the local Arab peasants, and massacres of Christian and Jewish communities by the rebels. Following the revolt, Muhammad Pasha, the son of Muhammad Ali, expelled nearly 10,000 of the local peasants to Egypt, while bringing loyal Arab peasants from Egypt and discharged soldiers to settle the coastline of Ottoman Syria. Northern
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Valley_(Middle_East)" title="Jordan Valley (Middle East)">
       Jordan Valley
      </a>
      was settled by his Sudanese troops.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1838 there was another
      <a href="/wiki/1838_Druze_revolt" title="1838 Druze revolt">
       revolt
      </a>
      by the Druze. In 1839
      <a href="/wiki/Moses_Montefiore" title="Moses Montefiore">
       Moses Montefiore
      </a>
      met with Muhammed Pasha in Egypt and signed an agreement to establish 100-200 Jewish villages in the
      <a href="/wiki/Damascus_Eyalet" title="Damascus Eyalet">
       Damascus Eyalet
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Syria" title="Ottoman Syria">
       Ottoman Syria
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but in 1840 the Egyptians withdrew before the deal was implemented, returning the area to Ottoman governorship. In 1844, Jews constituted the largest population group in Jerusalem and by 1890 an absolute majority in the city, but as a whole the Jewish population made up far less than 10% of the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1868, the Ottomans banished the
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27u%27ll%C3%A1h" title="Bah'u'llh">
       Bah'u'llh
      </a>
      , one of the founders of the Bah' Faith, to Acre where he is buried, and the movement subsequently established its global administrative centre in nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
       Haifa
      </a>
      . In 1874, Ottoman reforms led to the area of Jerusalem gaining special status as the
      <a href="/wiki/Mutasarrifate_of_Jerusalem" title="Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem">
       Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_Zionism_1870.E2.80.931914">
       Birth of Zionism 18701914
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Birth of Zionism 18701914">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Zionism" title="History of Zionism">
       History of Zionism
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Mutasarrifate_of_Jerusalem" title="Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem">
       Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem
      </a>
     </div>

       <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">

          </a>
         </li>

          <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">

          </a>

          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Yerida" title="Yerida">
           Yerida
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Homeland_for_the_Jewish_people" title="Homeland for the Jewish people">
           Homeland for the Jewish people
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Jewish_messianism" title="Jewish messianism">
           Jewish messianism
          </a>
         </li>

        </ul>
       </td>
      </tr>

      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;font-weight:bold;">
        <img alt="Category" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="36" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/16px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/24px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/32px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 2x" title="Category" width="16"/>
        <a href="/wiki/Category:Aliyah" title="Category:Aliyah">
         Category
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Aliyah" title="Template:Aliyah">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Aliyah" title="Template talk:Aliyah">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Aliyah&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      During the 19th century, Jews in Western Europe were increasingly granted citizenship and
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_emancipation" title="Jewish emancipation">
       equality before the law
      </a>
      ; however, in Eastern Europe, they faced growing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_zionism#Persecution_in_Russia_.28before_the_revolution.29" title="History of zionism">
       persecution and legal restrictions
      </a>
      , including widespread
      <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">
       pogroms
      </a>
      . Half the world's Jews lived in the Russian Empire, where they were regarded as a separate national group and restricted to living in the
      <a href="/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement" title="Pale of Settlement">
       Pale of Settlement
      </a>
      . National groups in the Empire, such as the Poles, Lithuanians and Ukrainians were agitating for independence and regarded as aliens the Jews, who were usually the only non-Christian minority and spoke a distinct language (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">
       Yiddish
      </a>
      ). An independent Jewish national movement first began to emerge in the Russian Empire and the millions of Jews who were fleeing the country (mostly to the USA) carried the seeds of this nationalism wherever they went.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1870, an agricultural school, the
      <a href="/wiki/Mikveh_Israel" title="Mikveh Israel">
       Mikveh Israel
      </a>
      , was founded near
      <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">
       Jaffa
      </a>
      by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alliance_Israelite_Universelle" title="Alliance Israelite Universelle">
       Alliance Israelite Universelle
      </a>
      , a French Jewish association. In 1878, "Russian" Jewish emigrants established the village of
      <a href="/wiki/Petah_Tikva" title="Petah Tikva">
       Petah Tikva
      </a>
      , followed by
      <a href="/wiki/Rishon_LeZion" title="Rishon LeZion">
       Rishon LeZion
      </a>
      in 1882. "Russian" Jews established the
      <a href="/wiki/Bilu" title="Bilu">
       Bilu
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hovevei_Zion" title="Hovevei Zion">
       Hovevei Zion
      </a>
      ("Love of Zion") movements to assist settlers and these created additional communities that, unlike the traditional Ashkenazi-Jewish communities, sought to be self-reliant rather than dependent on donations from abroad. Existing Ashkenazi-Jewish communities were concentrated in the
      <a href="/wiki/Four_Holy_Cities" title="Four Holy Cities">
       Four Holy Cities
      </a>
      , extremely poor and lived on donations from Europe. The new migrants avoided these communities and tended to create small agricultural settlements. In Jaffa a vibrant commercial community developed in which Ashkenazi and Sephardi Jews inter-mingled. Many early migrants left due to difficulty finding work and the early settlements often remained dependent on foreign donations. Despite the difficulties, more settlements arose and the community continued to grow.
     </p>
     <p>
      The new migration was accompanied by a
      <a href="/wiki/Revival_of_the_Hebrew_language" title="Revival of the Hebrew language">
       revival of the Hebrew language
      </a>
      and attracted Jews of all kinds; religious, secular, nationalists and
      <a href="/wiki/Labor_Zionism" title="Labor Zionism">
       left-wing socialists
      </a>
      . Socialists aimed to reclaim the land by becoming peasants or workers and forming
      <a href="/wiki/Kibbutz" title="Kibbutz">
       collectives
      </a>
      . In Zionist history, the different waves of Jewish settlement are known as "
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah" title="Aliyah">
       aliyah
      </a>
      ". During the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Aliyah" title="First Aliyah">
       First Aliyah
      </a>
      , between 1882 and 1903, approximately 35,000 Jews moved to what is now Israel. The first wave coincided with a wave of Jewish migration and
      <a href="/wiki/Messianism" title="Messianism">
       Messianism
      </a>
      among
      <a href="/wiki/Yemenite_Jews" title="Yemenite Jews">
       Yemenite Jews
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bukharan_Jews" title="Bukharan Jews">
       Bukharan Jews
      </a>
      . By 1890, Jews were a majority in
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      , although the country as a whole was populated mainly by Muslim (settled and nomad Bedouins) and Christian Arabs.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1896
      <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Herzl" title="Theodor Herzl">
       Theodor Herzl
      </a>
      published
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Der_Judenstaat" title="Der Judenstaat">
        Der Judenstaat
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       The Jewish State
      </i>
      ), in which he asserted that the solution to growing
      <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">
       antisemitism
      </a>
      in Europe (the so-called "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Question" title="Jewish Question">
       Jewish Question
      </a>
      ") was to establish a Jewish state. In 1897, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zionist_Organisation" title="Zionist Organisation">
       Zionist Organisation
      </a>
      was founded and the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Zionist_Congress" title="First Zionist Congress">
       First Zionist Congress
      </a>
      proclaimed its aim "to establish a home for the Jewish people in Palestine secured under public law."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, Zionism was regarded with suspicion by the Ottoman rulers and was unable to make major progress.
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1904 and 1914, around 40,000 Jews settled in Southern Syria (the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Aliyah" title="Second Aliyah">
       Second Aliyah
      </a>
      ). In 1908 the Zionist Organisation set up the Palestine Bureau (also known as the "Eretz Israel Office") in Jaffa and began to adopt a systematic Jewish settlement policy. Migrants were mainly from Russia (which then included part of Poland), escaping persecution. The first
      <a href="/wiki/Kibbutz" title="Kibbutz">
       Kibbutz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Degania_Alef" title="Degania Alef">
       Degania
      </a>
      , was founded by nine Russian socialists in 1909. In 1909 residents of Jaffa established the first entirely Hebrew-speaking city,
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv#Ahuzat_Bayit" title="Tel Aviv">
       Ahuzat Bayit
      </a>
      (later renamed
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      ). Hebrew newspapers and books were published,
      <a href="/wiki/Herzliya_Hebrew_Gymnasium" title="Herzliya Hebrew Gymnasium">
       Hebrew schools
      </a>
      , Jewish political parties and workers organizations were established.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_1914.E2.80.931917">
       World War I 19141917
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: World War I 19141917">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Occupied_Enemy_Territory_Administration" title="Occupied Enemy Territory Administration">
       Occupied Enemy Territory Administration
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration" title="Balfour Declaration">
       Balfour Declaration
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sykes-Picot.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="800" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sykes-Picot.svg/170px-Sykes-Picot.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sykes-Picot.svg/255px-Sykes-Picot.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Sykes-Picot.svg/340px-Sykes-Picot.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sykes-Picot.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        French and British influence and control (
        <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="SykesPicot Agreement">
         SykesPicot Agreement
        </a>
        , 1916)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
       World War I
      </a>
      , most Jews supported the Germans because they were fighting the Russians who were regarded as the Jews' main enemy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Britain, the government sought Jewish support for the war effort for a variety of reasons including an erroneous antisemitic perception of "Jewish power" over the Ottoman Empire's
      <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">
       Young Turks
      </a>
      movement,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a desire to secure American Jewish support for US intervention on Britain's behalf.
     </p>
     <p>
      There was already sympathy for the aims of
      <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">
       Zionism
      </a>
      in the British government, including the Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">
       Lloyd George
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In late 1917, the British Army drove the Turks
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_and_Palestine_Campaign#Palestine_campaign" title="Sinai and Palestine Campaign">
       out of Southern Syria
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the British foreign minister,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Balfour" title="Lord Balfour">
       Lord Balfour
      </a>
      , sent a public letter to
      <a href="/wiki/Walter_Rothschild,_2nd_Baron_Rothschild" title="Walter Rothschild, 2nd Baron Rothschild">
       Lord Rothschild
      </a>
      , a leading member of his party and leader of the Jewish community. The letter subsequently became known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1917" title="Balfour Declaration of 1917">
       Balfour Declaration of 1917
      </a>
      . It stated that the British Government "view[ed] with favour the establishment in
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">
       Palestine
      </a>
      of a national home for the Jewish people". The declaration provided the British government with a pretext for claiming and governing the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      New Middle Eastern boundaries were decided
      <a href="/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement" title="SykesPicot Agreement">
       by an agreement
      </a>
      between British and French bureaucrats. The agreement gave Britain control over what parties would begin to call "Palestine". This appellation would remain uncontroversial until the rise of
      <a href="/wiki/Anti-Zionism" title="Anti-Zionism">
       Anti-Zionism
      </a>
      in the 1940s.
     </p>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Legion" title="Jewish Legion">
       Jewish Legion
      </a>
      composed largely of Zionist volunteers organized by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabotinsky" title="Jabotinsky">
       Jabotinsky
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trumpeldor" title="Trumpeldor">
       Trumpeldor
      </a>
      participated in the British invasion. It also participated in the failed
      <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_Campaign" title="Gallipoli Campaign">
       Gallipoli Campaign
      </a>
      . A
      <a href="/wiki/Nili" title="Nili">
       Zionist spy network
      </a>
      provided the British with details of Ottoman troops.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="British_Mandate_of_Palestine_.281920.E2.80.931948.29">
       British Mandate of Palestine (19201948)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: British Mandate of Palestine (19201948)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">
       Mandatory Palestine
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="First_years_1920.E2.80.931929">
       First years 19201929
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: First years 19201929">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency_for_Israel" title="Jewish Agency for Israel">
       Jewish Agency for Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="862" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG/220px-Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG/330px-Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG/440px-Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balfour_portrait_and_declaration.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration" title="Balfour Declaration">
         Balfour Declaration
        </a>
        of 1917, which supported the establishment of a Jewish homeland in Palestine
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/British_Mandate_for_Palestine_(legal_instrument)" title="British Mandate for Palestine (legal instrument)">
       British Mandate
      </a>
      (in effect, British rule) of Palestine, including the Balfour Declaration, was confirmed by the
      <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
       League of Nations
      </a>
      in 1922 and came into effect in 1923. The boundaries of Palestine initially included modern
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Jordan
      </a>
      , which was
      <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">
       removed
      </a>
      from the territory by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Churchill" title="Churchill">
       Churchill
      </a>
      a few years later. Britain signed a treaty with the United States (which did not join the League of Nations) in which the United States endorsed the terms of the Mandate.
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1919 and 1923, another 40,000 Jews arrived in Palestine, mainly escaping the post-
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">
       revolutionary
      </a>
      chaos of Russia (
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Aliyah" title="Third Aliyah">
       Third Aliyah
      </a>
      ), as over 100,000 Jews were massacred in this period in Ukraine and Russia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many of these immigrants became known as "
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pioneer" title="wikt:pioneer">
       pioneers
      </a>
      " (halutzim), experienced or trained in agriculture and capable of establishing self-sustaining economies. The
      <a href="/wiki/Jezreel_Valley" title="Jezreel Valley">
       Jezreel Valley
      </a>
      and the Hefer Plain marshes were drained and converted to agricultural use. Land was bought by the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Fund" title="Jewish National Fund">
       Jewish National Fund
      </a>
      , a Zionist charity that collected money abroad for that purpose. A mainly socialist underground Jewish militia,
      <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">
       Haganah
      </a>
      ("Defense"), was established to defend outlying Jewish settlements.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3559" data-file-width="2615" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg/170px-Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg/255px-Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg/340px-Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Founding_of_the_Hebrew_University.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The opening ceremony of The
        <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem" title="Hebrew University of Jerusalem">
         Hebrew University of Jerusalem
        </a>
        visited by
        <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Balfour" title="Arthur Balfour">
         Arthur Balfour
        </a>
        , 1 April 1925
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The French
      <a href="/wiki/Franco-Syrian_War" title="Franco-Syrian War">
       victory
      </a>
      over the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Kingdom_of_Syria" title="Arab Kingdom of Syria">
       Arab Kingdom of Syria
      </a>
      and the Balfour Declaration led to the emergence of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Nationalism" title="Palestinian Nationalism">
       Palestinian Nationalism
      </a>
      and Arab rioting in
      <a href="/wiki/1920_Nebi_Musa_riots" title="1920 Nebi Musa riots">
       1920
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jaffa_riots" title="Jaffa riots">
       1921
      </a>
      . In response, the British authorities imposed immigration quotas for Jews. Exceptions were made for Jews with over 1,000 pounds in cash (roughly 100,000 pounds at year 2000 rates) or Jewish professionals with over 500 pounds. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency" title="Jewish Agency">
       Jewish Agency
      </a>
      issued the British entry permits and distributed funds donated by Jews abroad.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between 1924 and 1929, 82,000 more Jews arrived (
      <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Aliyah" title="Fourth Aliyah">
       Fourth Aliyah
      </a>
      ), fleeing antisemitism in Poland and Hungary, and because the United States
      <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1924" title="Immigration Act of 1924">
       Immigration Act of 1924
      </a>
      now kept Jews out. The new arrivals included many middle-class families who moved into towns and established small businesses and workshopsalthough lack of economic opportunities meant that approximately a quarter later left. The first electricity generator was built in Tel Aviv in 1923 under the guidance of
      <a href="/wiki/Pinhas_Rutenberg" title="Pinhas Rutenberg">
       Pinhas Rutenberg
      </a>
      , a former
      <a href="/wiki/Commissar" title="Commissar">
       Commissar
      </a>
      of St Petersburg in Russia's pre-Bolshevik
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerensky_Government" title="Kerensky Government">
       Kerensky Government
      </a>
      . In 1925 the Jewish Agency established the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew_University" title="Hebrew University">
       Hebrew University
      </a>
      in Jerusalem and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technion" title="Technion">
       Technion
      </a>
      (technological university) in Haifa.
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1928, the democratically elected Va'ad Leumi (
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_National_Council" title="Jewish National Council">
       Jewish National Council
      </a>
      or JNC) became the main institution of the Palestine Jewish community ("
      <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">
       Yishuv
      </a>
      ") and included non-Zionist Jews. As the Yishuv grew, the JNC adopted more government-type functions, such as education, health care and security. With British permission, the Va'ad raised its own taxes
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and ran independent services for the Jewish population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      From 1929 its leadership was elected by Jews from 26 countries.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1929 tensions grew over the Kotel (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wailing_Wall" title="Wailing Wall">
       Wailing Wall
      </a>
      ), a narrow alleyway where Jews were banned from using chairs or any furniture (many of the worshipers were elderly). The
      <a href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">
       Mufti
      </a>
      claimed it was Muslim property and that the Jews were seeking control of the Temple Mount. This (and general animosity) led to the August
      <a href="/wiki/1929_Palestine_riots" title="1929 Palestine riots">
       1929 Palestine riots
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/1929_Hebron_massacre" title="1929 Hebron massacre">
       main victims
      </a>
      were the ancient Jewish community at Hebron, which came to an end. The riots led to right-wing Zionists establishing their own militia in 1931, the
      <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
       Irgun
      </a>
      Tzvai Leumi (National Military Organization, known in Hebrew by its acronym "Etzel").
     </p>
     <p>
      Zionist political parties provided private education and health care: the
      <a href="/wiki/General_Zionists" title="General Zionists">
       General Zionists
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Mizrachi_(political_party)" title="Mizrachi (political party)">
       Mizrahi
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Labor_Zionism" title="Labor Zionism">
       Socialist Zionists
      </a>
      , each established independent health and education services and operated sports organizations funded by local taxes, donations and fees (the British administration did not invest in public services). During the whole interwar period, the British, appealing to the terms of the Mandate, rejected the principle of majority rule or any other measure that would give the Arab population, who formed the majority of the population, control over Palestinian territory.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Increase_of_Jewish_immigration_1930.E2.80.931938">
       Increase of Jewish immigration 19301938
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Increase of Jewish immigration 19301938">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Aliyah" title="Fifth Aliyah">
       Fifth Aliyah
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">
       Nuremberg Laws
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1933, the Jewish Agency and the Nazis negotiated the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ha%27avara_Agreement" title="Ha'avara Agreement">
       Ha'avara Agreement
      </a>
      (transfer agreement), under which 50,000 Jews would be transferred to Palestine. The Jews possessions were confiscated and in return the Nazis allowed the Ha'avara organization to purchase 14 million pounds worth of German goods for export to Palestine (which was used to compensate the immigrants). The Nazis did not normally allow Jews to leave with any money or to take more than two suitcases. The agreement was controversial and the Labour Zionist leader who negotiated the agreement,
      <a href="/wiki/Haim_Arlosoroff" title="Haim Arlosoroff">
       Haim Arlosoroff
      </a>
      , was assassinated in Tel Aviv in 1933. The assassination was a long source of anger between the Zionist left and Zionist right. Arlosoroff once dated
      <a href="/wiki/Magda_Goebbels" title="Magda Goebbels">
       Magda Goebbels
      </a>
      and may have been assassinated by the Nazis to hide the connection, which only emerged recently. In Palestine, Jewish immigration (and the Ha'avara goods) helped the economy to flourish. A port and oil refineries were built at Haifa and there was a growth of industrialization in the predominantly agricultural Palestinian economy.
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1929 and 1938, 250,000 Jews arrived in Palestine (
      <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Aliyah" title="Fifth Aliyah">
       Fifth Aliyah
      </a>
      ). 174,000 arrived between 1933 and 1936, after which the British increasingly restricted immigration. The influx contributed to the
      <a href="/wiki/1933_Palestine_riots" title="1933 Palestine riots">
       1933 Palestine riots
      </a>
      . Migration was mostly from Europe and included professionals, doctors, lawyers and professors from Germany. As a consequence German architects of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bauhaus" title="Bauhaus">
       Bauhaus
      </a>
      school made Tel-Aviv the world's only city with purely
      <a href="/wiki/White_City_(Tel_Aviv)" title="White City (Tel Aviv)">
       Bauhaus neighborhoods
      </a>
      and Palestine had the highest per-capita percentage of doctors in the world.
     </p>
     <p>
      As Fascist regimes emerged across Europe, persecution of Jews massively increased, and Jews reverted to being non-citizens deprived of civil and economic rights, subject to arbitrary persecution. Significantly antisemitic governments came to power in
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">
       Poland
      </a>
      (from 1935 the government boycotted Jews),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungary_during_World_War_II" title="Hungary during World War II">
       Hungary
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Romania_in_World_War_II" title="Romania in World War II">
       Romania
      </a>
      and the Nazi created states of
      <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">
       Croatia
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (19391945)">
       Slovakia
      </a>
      , while
      <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
       Germany
      </a>
      annexed
      <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">
       Austria
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">
       Czech territories
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_revolt_and_the_White_Paper">
       Arab revolt and the White Paper
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Arab revolt and the White Paper">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
       19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939" title="White Paper of 1939">
       White Paper of 1939
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3538" data-file-width="4797" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg/220px-Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg/330px-Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg/440px-Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ghaffis_in_Nesher_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Settlement_Police" title="Jewish Settlement Police">
         Jewish Settlement Police
        </a>
        members watching the settlement
        <a href="/wiki/Nesher" title="Nesher">
         Nesher
        </a>
        during
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
         19361939 Arab revolt
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Jewish immigration and Nazi propaganda contributed to the large-scale
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine" title="19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine">
       19361939 Arab revolt in Palestine
      </a>
      , a largely nationalist uprising directed at ending British rule. The head of the Jewish Agency, Ben-Gurion, responded to the Arab Revolt with a policy of "
      <a href="/wiki/Havlagah" title="Havlagah">
       Havlagah
      </a>
      "self-restraint and a refusal to be provoked by Arab attacks in order to prevent polarization. The Etzel group broke off from the Haganah in opposition to this policy.
     </p>
     <p>
      The British responded to the revolt with the
      <a href="/wiki/Peel_Commission" title="Peel Commission">
       Peel Commission
      </a>
      (193637), a public inquiry that recommended that an exclusively Jewish territory be created in the
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      and western coast (including the
      <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer" title="Population transfer">
       population transfer
      </a>
      of 225,000 Arabs); the rest becoming an exclusively Arab area. The two main Jewish leaders,
      <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">
       Chaim Weizmann
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      , had convinced the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Zionist_Congress" title="World Zionist Congress">
       Zionist Congress
      </a>
      to approve equivocally the Peel recommendations as a basis for more negotiation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The plan was rejected outright by the Palestinian Arab leadership and they renewed the revolt, which caused the British to appease the Arabs, and to abandon the plan as unworkable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Testifying before the Peel Commission, Weizmann said "There are in Europe 6,000,000 people ... for whom the world is divided into places where they cannot live and places where they cannot enter." In 1938, the US called an
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vian_Conference" title="vian Conference">
       international conference
      </a>
      to address the question of the vast numbers of Jews trying to escape Europe. Britain made its attendance contingent on Palestine being kept out of the discussion. No Jewish representatives were invited. The Nazis proposed their own solution: that the Jews of Europe be shipped to Madagascar (the
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_Plan" title="Madagascar Plan">
       Madagascar Plan
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      With millions of Jews trying to leave Europe and every country in the world closed to Jewish migration, the British decided to close Palestine. The
      <a href="/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939" title="White Paper of 1939">
       White Paper of 1939
      </a>
      , recommended that an independent Palestine, governed jointly by Arabs and Jews, be established within 10 years. The White Paper agreed to allow 75,000 Jewish immigrants into Palestine over the period 194044, after which migration would require Arab approval. Both the Arab and Jewish leadership rejected the White Paper. In March 1940 the British High Commissioner for Palestine issued an edict banning Jews from purchasing land in 95% of Palestine. Jews now resorted to illegal immigration: (
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah_Bet" title="Aliyah Bet">
       Aliyah Bet
      </a>
      or "Ha'apalah"), often organized by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mossad_Le%27aliyah_Bet" title="Mossad Le'aliyah Bet">
       Mossad Le'aliyah Bet
      </a>
      and the Irgun. Very few Jews managed to escape Europe between 1939 and 1945. Those caught by the British were mostly
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Mauritius" title="History of the Jews in Mauritius">
       sent to Mauritius
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_the_Holocaust">
       World War II and the Holocaust
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
