       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: World War II and the Holocaust">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah_Bet" title="Aliyah Bet">
       Aliyah Bet
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_during_World_War_II" title="History of the Jews during World War II">
       History of the Jews during World War II
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
       The Holocaust
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Italian_bombing_of_Mandatory_Palestine_in_World_War_II" title="Italian bombing of Mandatory Palestine in World War II">
       Italian bombing of Mandatory Palestine in World War II
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JB_HQ.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="177" data-file-width="257" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg/220px-JB_HQ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bb/JB_HQ.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JB_HQ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Brigade" title="Jewish Brigade">
         Jewish Brigade
        </a>
        headquarters under both
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Flag" title="Union Flag">
         Union Flag
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Israel" title="Flag of Israel">
         Jewish flag
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2nd_World_War" title="2nd World War">
       2nd World War
      </a>
      , the Jewish Agency worked to establish a Jewish army that would fight alongside the British forces. Churchill supported the plan but British Military and government opposition led to its rejection. The British demanded that the number of Jewish recruits match the number of Palestinian Arab recruits,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but few Arabs would fight for Britain, and the Palestinian leader, the
      <a href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">
       Mufti of Jerusalem
      </a>
      , joined the Nazis in Europe.
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 1941, the
      <a href="/wiki/Palmach" title="Palmach">
       Palmach
      </a>
      was established to defend the
      <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">
       Yishuv
      </a>
      against the planned
      <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">
       Axis
      </a>
      invasion through
      <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">
       North Africa
      </a>
      . The British refusal to provide arms to the Jews, even when Rommel's forces were
      <a href="/wiki/200_days_of_dread" title="200 days of dread">
       advancing through Egypt
      </a>
      in June 1942 (intent on occupying Palestine) and the 1939 White Paper, led to the emergence of a Zionist leadership in Palestine that believed conflict with Britain was inevitable.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Despite this, the Jewish Agency called on Palestine's Jewish youth to volunteer for the British Army (both men and women). 30,000 Palestinian Jews
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 6,000 Palestinian Arabs
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      enlisted in the British armed forces during the war. In June 1944 the British agreed to create a
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Brigade" title="Jewish Brigade">
       Jewish Brigade
      </a>
      that would fight in Italy.
     </p>
     <p>
      Approximately 1.5 million Jews around the world served in every branch of the allied armies, mainly in the Soviet and U.S. armies. 200,000 Jews died serving in the Soviet army alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many of these war veterans later volunteered to fight for Israel or were active in its support.
     </p>
     <p>
      A small group (about 200 activists), dedicated to resisting the British administration in Palestine, broke away from the Etzel (which advocated support for Britain during the war) and formed the "Lehi" (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stern_Gang" title="Stern Gang">
       Stern Gang
      </a>
      ), led by
      <a href="/wiki/Avraham_Stern" title="Avraham Stern">
       Avraham Stern
      </a>
      . In 1943, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">
       USSR
      </a>
      released the Revisionist Zionist leader
      <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
       Menachem Begin
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">
       Gulag
      </a>
      and he went to Palestine, taking command of the Etzel organization with a policy of increased conflict against the British. At about the same time
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Shamir" title="Yitzhak Shamir">
       Yitzhak Shamir
      </a>
      escaped from the
      <a href="/wiki/Irgun_and_Lehi_internment_in_Africa" title="Irgun and Lehi internment in Africa">
       camp in Eritrea
      </a>
      where the British were holding Lehi activists without trial, taking command of the Lehi (Stern Gang).
     </p>
     <p>
      Jews in the Middle East were also affected by the war. Most of North Africa came under Nazi control and many Jews were used as slaves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 1941
      <a href="/wiki/1941_Iraqi_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1941 Iraqi coup d'tat">
       pro-Axis coup in Iraq
      </a>
      was accompanied by
      <a href="/wiki/Farhud" title="Farhud">
       massacres
      </a>
      of Jews. The Jewish Agency put together plans for a last stand in the event of Rommel invading Palestine (the Nazis planned to exterminate Palestine's Jews).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1939 and 1945, the Nazis,
      <a href="/wiki/Responsibility_for_the_Holocaust" title="Responsibility for the Holocaust">
       aided by local forces
      </a>
      , led systematic efforts to kill every person of Jewish extraction in Europe (The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
       Holocaust
      </a>
      ), causing the deaths of approximately 6 million Jews. A quarter of those killed were children. The Polish and German Jewish communities, which played an important role in defining the pre-1945 Jewish world, mostly ceased to exist. In the United States and Palestine, Jews of European origin became disconnected from their families and roots.
      <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
       Sepharadi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews" title="Mizrahi Jews">
       Mizrahi Jews
      </a>
      , who had been a minority, became a much more significant factor in the Jewish world. Those Jews who survived in central Europe, were
      <a href="/wiki/Displaced_persons_camp" title="Displaced persons camp">
       displaced persons
      </a>
      (refugees); an
      <a href="/wiki/Anglo-American_Committee_of_Inquiry" title="Anglo-American Committee of Inquiry">
       Anglo-American Committee of Inquiry
      </a>
      , established to examine the Palestine issue, surveyed their ambitions and found that over 95% wanted to migrate to Palestine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the Zionist movement the moderate Pro-British (and British citizen) Weizmann, whose son died flying in the
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">
       RAF
      </a>
      , was undermined by Britain's anti-Zionist policies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Leadership of the movement passed to the Jewish Agency in Palestine, now led by the anti-British Socialist-Zionist party (
      <a href="/wiki/Mapai" title="Mapai">
       Mapai
      </a>
      ) and led by
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      . In the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_diaspora" title="Jewish diaspora">
       diaspora
      </a>
      , U.S. Jews now dominated the Zionist movement.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Illegal_Jewish_immigration_and_insurgency">
       Illegal Jewish immigration and insurgency
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Illegal Jewish immigration and insurgency">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Bricha" title="Bricha">
       Bricha
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_insurgency_in_Palestine" title="Jewish insurgency in Palestine">
       Jewish insurgency in Palestine
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Jewish_violence_in_Poland,_1944-1946" title="Anti-Jewish violence in Poland, 1944-1946">
       Anti-Jewish violence in Poland, 1944-1946
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
       British Empire
      </a>
      was severely weakened by the war. In the Middle East, the war had made Britain conscious of its dependence on Arab oil. British firms controlled Iraqi oil and Britain ruled Kuwait, Bahrain and the Emirates. Shortly after
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VE_Day" title="VE Day">
       VE Day
      </a>
      , the Labour Party won the general election in Britain. Although Labour Party conferences had for years called for the establishment of a Jewish state in Palestine, the Labour government now decided to maintain the 1939 White Paper policies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="2508" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg/220px-19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg/330px-19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg/440px-19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:19450715_Buchenwald_survivors_arrive_in_Haifa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald_concentration_camp" title="Buchenwald concentration camp">
         Buchenwald
        </a>
        survivors arrive in
        <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
         Haifa
        </a>
        to be arrested by the British, 15 July 1945
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Illegal migration (
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah_Bet" title="Aliyah Bet">
       Aliyah Bet
      </a>
      ) became the main form of Jewish entry into Palestine. Across Europe
      <a href="/wiki/Bricha" title="Bricha">
       Bricha
      </a>
      ("flight"), an organization of former
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_partisans" title="Jewish partisans">
       partisans
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_resistance_under_Nazi_rule" title="Jewish resistance under Nazi rule">
       ghetto fighters
      </a>
      , smuggled Holocaust survivors from Eastern Europe to Mediterranean ports, where small boats tried to breach the British blockade of Palestine. Meanwhile, Jews from Arab countries began moving into Palestine overland. Despite British efforts to curb immigration, during the 14 years of the Aliyah Bet, over 110,000 Jews entered Palestine. By the end of World War II, the Jewish population of Palestine had increased to 33% of the total population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In an effort to win independence, Zionists now waged a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British%E2%80%93Zionist_conflict" title="BritishZionist conflict">
       guerrilla war
      </a>
      against the British. The main underground Jewish militia, the Haganah, formed an alliance called the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Resistance_Movement" title="Jewish Resistance Movement">
       Jewish Resistance Movement
      </a>
      with the Etzel and Stern Gang to fight the British. In June 1946, following instances of Jewish
      <a href="/wiki/Night_of_the_Bridges" title="Night of the Bridges">
       sabotage
      </a>
      , the British launched
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Agatha" title="Operation Agatha">
       Operation Agatha
      </a>
      , arresting 2700 Jews, including the leadership of the Jewish Agency, whose headquarters were raided. Those arrested were held without trial.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland#Postwar" title="History of the Jews in Poland">
       Poland
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kielce_Pogrom" title="Kielce Pogrom">
       Kielce Pogrom
      </a>
      (July 1946) led to a wave of Holocaust survivors fleeing Europe for Palestine. Between 1945 and 1948, 100,000120,000 Jews left Poland. Their departure was largely organized by Zionist activists in Poland under the umbrella of the semi-clandestine organization
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berihah" title="Berihah">
        Berihah
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Flight").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YV-archive3_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-YV-archive3-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Berihah
      </i>
      was also responsible for the organized emigration of Jews from
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Romania#Post-War" title="History of the Jews in Romania">
       Romania
      </a>
      , Hungary, Czechoslovakia and Yugoslavia, totaling 250,000 (including Poland) Holocaust survivors. The British imprisoned the Jews trying to enter Palestine in the
      <a href="/wiki/Atlit_detainee_camp" title="Atlit detainee camp">
       Atlit detainee camp
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_internment_camps" title="Cyprus internment camps">
       Cyprus internment camps
      </a>
      . Those held were mainly Holocaust survivors, including large numbers of children and orphans. In response to Cypriot fears that the Jews would never leave (since they lacked a state or documentation) and because the 75,000 quota established by the 1939 White Paper had never been filled, the British allowed the refugees to enter Palestine at a rate of 750 per month.
     </p>
     <p>
      The unified Jewish resistance movement broke up in July 1946, after Etzel
      <a href="/wiki/King_David_Hotel_bombing" title="King David Hotel bombing">
       bombed the British Military Headquarters
      </a>
      in the King David Hotel killing 91 people. In the days following the bombing, Tel Aviv was placed under curfew and over 120,000 Jews, nearly 20% of the Jewish population of Palestine, were questioned by the police. In the U.S., Congress criticized British handling of the situation and delayed loans that were vital to British post-war recovery. By 1947 the Labour Government was ready to refer the Palestine problem to the newly created United Nations.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_Partition_Plan">
       United Nations Partition Plan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: United Nations Partition Plan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Palestine" title="United Nations Special Committee on Palestine">
       United Nations Special Committee on Palestine
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">
       United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1147" data-file-width="627" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png/170px-UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png/255px-UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png/340px-UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN_Partition_Plan_For_Palestine_1947.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">
         United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine
        </a>
        , 1947
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 2 April 1947, the United Kingdom requested that the question of Palestine be handled by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations" title="General Assembly of the United Nations">
       General Assembly
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The General Assembly created a committee,
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Palestine" title="United Nations Special Committee on Palestine">
       United Nations Special Committee on Palestine
      </a>
      (UNSCOP), to report on "the question of Palestine".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In July 1947 the UNSCOP visited Palestine and met with Jewish and Zionist delegations. The
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">
       Arab Higher Committee
      </a>
      boycotted the meetings. During the visit the British Foreign Secretary
      <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bevin" title="Ernest Bevin">
       Ernest Bevin
      </a>
      ordered an illegal immigrant ship, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exodus_1947" title="Exodus 1947">
       Exodus 1947
      </a>
      , to be sent back to Europe. The migrants on the ship were forcibly removed by British troops at Hamburg.
     </p>
     <p>
      The principal non-Zionist Orthodox Jewish (or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haredi" title="Haredi">
       Haredi
      </a>
      ) party,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agudat_Israel" title="Agudat Israel">
       Agudat Israel
      </a>
      , recommended to UNSCOP that a Jewish state be set up after reaching a religious
      <a href="/wiki/Status_quo_(Israel)" title="Status quo (Israel)">
       status quo agreement
      </a>
      with Ben-Gurion regarding the future Jewish state. The agreement would grant exemption to a quota of
      <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva" title="Yeshiva">
       yeshiva
      </a>
      (religious seminary) students and to all orthodox women from military service, would make the Sabbath the national weekend, promised
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kosher" title="Kosher">
       Kosher
      </a>
      food in government institutions and would allow them to maintain a separate education system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The majority report of UNSCOP proposed
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "an independent Arab State, an independent Jewish State, and the City of Jerusalem" ..., the last to be under "an International Trusteeship System".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 29 November 1947, in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resolution_181" title="Resolution 181">
       Resolution 181
      </a>
      (II), the General Assembly adopted the majority report of UNSCOP, but with slight modifications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Plan also called for the British to allow "substantial" Jewish migration by 1 February 1948.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Neither Britain nor the UN Security Council took any action to implement the resolution and Britain continued detaining Jews attempting to enter Palestine. Concerned that partition would severely damage Anglo-Arab relations, Britain denied UN representatives access to Palestine during the period between the adoption of Resolution 181 (II) and the termination of the British Mandate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The British withdrawal was finally completed in May 1948. However, Britain continued to hold Jews of "fighting age" and their families on Cyprus until March 1949.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">
       Civil War
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Civil War">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_Civil_War_in_Mandatory_Palestine" title="19471948 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine">
       19471948 Civil War in Mandatory Palestine
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The General Assembly's vote caused joy in the Jewish community and discontent among the Arab community. Violence broke out between the sides. From January 1948, operations became increasingly militarized, with the intervention of a number of
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Liberation_Army" title="Arab Liberation Army">
       Arab Liberation Army
      </a>
      regiments inside Palestine, each active in a variety of distinct sectors around the different coastal towns. They consolidated their presence in
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Samaria" title="Samaria">
       Samaria
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yoav_Gelber_2006_pp.51-56_103-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Yoav_Gelber_2006_pp.51-56-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Qadir_al-Husayni" title="Abd al-Qadir al-Husayni">
       Abd al-Qadir al-Husayni
      </a>
      came from Egypt with several hundred men of the
      <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Holy_War" title="Army of the Holy War">
       Army of the Holy War
      </a>
      . Having recruited a few thousand volunteers, he organized the blockade of the 100,000 Jewish residents of Jerusalem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larry_Collins_1971_p.7_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Larry_Collins_1971_p.7-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Yishuv" title="Yishuv">
       Yishuv
      </a>
      tried to supply the city using convoys of up to 100 armoured vehicles, but largely failed. By March, almost all
      <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">
       Haganah
      </a>
      's armoured vehicles had been destroyed, the blockade was in full operation, and hundreds of Haganah members who had tried to bring supplies into the city were killed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benny_Morris_2003_p.163_105-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Benny_Morris_2003_p.163-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Up to 100,000 Arabs, from the urban upper and middle classes in Haifa, Jaffa and Jerusalem, or Jewish-dominated areas, evacuated abroad or to Arab centres eastwards.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benny_Morris_2003_p.67_106-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Benny_Morris_2003_p.67-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This situation caused the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US" title="US">
       US
      </a>
      to withdraw their support for the Partition plan, thus encouraging the
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
       Arab League
      </a>
      to believe that the Palestinian Arabs, reinforced by the Arab Liberation Army, could put an end to the plan for partition. The British, on the other hand, decided on 7 February 1948 to support the annexation of the Arab part of Palestine by
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Transjordan
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henry_Laurens_2005_p.83_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Henry_Laurens_2005_p.83-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jerusalem_convoy.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1948" data-file-width="1640" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Jerusalem_convoy.jpg/170px-Jerusalem_convoy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Jerusalem_convoy.jpg/255px-Jerusalem_convoy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Jerusalem_convoy.jpg/340px-Jerusalem_convoy.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jerusalem_convoy.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Supply convoy on its way to
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_for_Jerusalem_(1948)" title="Battle for Jerusalem (1948)">
         besieged
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
         Jerusalem
        </a>
        , April 1948
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      reorganized Haganah and made conscription obligatory. Every Jewish man and woman in the country had to receive military training. Thanks to funds raised by
      <a href="/wiki/Golda_Meir" title="Golda Meir">
       Golda Meir
      </a>
      from sympathisers in the United States, and Stalin's decision to support the
      <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">
       Zionist
      </a>
      cause, the Jewish representatives of Palestine were able to purchase important arms in Eastern Europe.
     </p>
     <p>
      Ben-Gurion gave
      <a href="/wiki/Yigael_Yadin" title="Yigael Yadin">
       Yigael Yadin
      </a>
      the responsibility to plan for the announced intervention of the Arab states. The result of his analysis was
      <a href="/wiki/Plan_Dalet" title="Plan Dalet">
       Plan Dalet
      </a>
      , in which Haganah passed from the defensive to the offensive. The plan sought to establish Jewish territorial continuity by conquering mixed zones.
      <a href="/wiki/Tiberias" title="Tiberias">
       Tiberias
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">
       Haifa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Safed" title="Safed">
       Safed
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beisan" title="Beisan">
       Beisan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jaffa" title="Jaffa">
       Jaffa
      </a>
      and Acre fell, resulting in the flight of more than 250,000 Palestinian Arabs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The situation pushed the leaders of the neighbouring Arab states to intervene.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 14 May 1948, on the day the last British forces left from Haifa, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_People%27s_Council" title="Jewish People's Council">
       Jewish People's Council
      </a>
      gathered at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_Museum" title="Tel Aviv Museum">
       Tel Aviv Museum
      </a>
      and proclaimed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Establishment_of_State_of_Israel" title="Declaration of Establishment of State of Israel">
       the establishment
      </a>
      of a
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_state" title="Jewish state">
       Jewish state
      </a>
      in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eretz_Israel" title="Eretz Israel">
       Eretz Israel
      </a>
      , to be known as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">
       State of Israel
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Israel_.281948.E2.80.93present.29">
       State of Israel (1948present)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: State of Israel (1948present)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_Independence">
       War of Independence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: War of Independence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 ArabIsraeli War">
       1948 ArabIsraeli War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_(Eilat).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2821" data-file-width="1844" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg/170px-Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg/255px-Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg/340px-Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_%28Eilat%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_(Eilat).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Avraham_Adan" title="Avraham Adan">
         Avraham Adan
        </a>
        raising the
        <a href="/wiki/Ink_Flag" title="Ink Flag">
         Ink Flag
        </a>
        marking the end of the
        <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 ArabIsraeli War">
         1948 ArabIsraeli War
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Immediately following the declaration of the new state, both
      <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">
       superpower
      </a>
      leaders, U.S. President
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">
       Harry S. Truman
      </a>
      and Soviet leader
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
       Joseph Stalin
      </a>
      , recognized the new state. The
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
       Arab League
      </a>
      members Egypt, Transjordan, Syria, Lebanon and Iraq refused to accept the UN partition plan and proclaimed the right of self-determination for the Arabs across the whole of Palestine. The Arab states marched their forces into what had, until the previous day, been the British Mandate for Palestine, starting the
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 ArabIsraeli War">
       first ArabIsraeli War
      </a>
      . The Arab states had heavy military equipment at their disposal and were initially on the offensive. On 29 May 1948, the British initiated
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_50" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 50">
       United Nations Security Council Resolution 50
      </a>
      declaring an arms embargo on the region.
      <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
       Czechoslovakia
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arms_shipments_from_Czechoslovakia_to_Israel_1947%E2%80%931949" title="Arms shipments from Czechoslovakia to Israel 19471949">
       violated the resolution
      </a>
      supplying the Jewish state with critical military hardware to match the (mainly British) heavy equipment and planes already owned by the invading Arab states. On 11 June, a month-long UN truce was put into effect.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following independence, the
      <a href="/wiki/Haganah" title="Haganah">
       Haganah
      </a>
      became the
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">
       Israel Defense Forces
      </a>
      (IDF). The
      <a href="/wiki/Palmach" title="Palmach">
       Palmach
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Irgun" title="Irgun">
       Etzel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lehi_(group)" title="Lehi (group)">
       Lehi
      </a>
      were required to cease independent operations and join the IDF. During the ceasefire, Etzel attempted to bring in a private arms shipment aboard a ship called "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altalena" title="Altalena">
       Altalena
      </a>
      ". When they refused to hand the arms to the government, Ben-Gurion ordered that the ship be sunk. Several Etzel members were killed in the fighting.
     </p>
     <p>
      Large numbers of Jewish immigrants, many of them World War II veterans and Holocaust survivors, now began arriving in the new state of Israel, and many joined the IDF.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After an initial loss of territory by the Jewish state and its occupation by the Arab armies, from July the tide gradually turned in the Israelis' favour and they pushed the Arab armies out and conquered some of the territory that had been included in the proposed Arab state. At the end of November, tenuous local ceasefires were arranged between the Israelis, Syrians and Lebanese. On 1 December
      <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan" title="Abdullah I of Jordan">
       King Abdullah
      </a>
      announced the union of Transjordan with Arab Palestine west of the Jordan; only Britain recognized the annexation.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Armistice_Agreements">
       Armistice Agreements
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Armistice Agreements">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
       1949 Armistice Agreements
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cia-is-map2.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="330" height="368" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Cia-is-map2.png/170px-Cia-is-map2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Cia-is-map2.png/255px-Cia-is-map2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/Cia-is-map2.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cia-is-map2.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel)" title="Green Line (Israel)">
         1949 Green Line
        </a>
        borders
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Israel signed
      <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
       armistices
      </a>
      with Egypt (24 February), Lebanon (23 March), Jordan (3 April) and Syria (20 July). No actual peace agreements were signed. With
      <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
       permanent ceasefire
      </a>
      coming into effect, Israel's new borders, later known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel)" title="Green Line (Israel)">
       Green Line
      </a>
      , were established. These borders were not recognized by the Arab states as international boundaries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The IDF had overrun
      <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">
       Galilee
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jezreel_Valley" title="Jezreel Valley">
       Jezreel Valley
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/West_Jerusalem" title="West Jerusalem">
       West Jerusalem
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain" title="Israeli coastal plain">
       coastal plain
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">
       Negev
      </a>
      . The Syrians remained in control of a strip of territory along the Sea of Galilee originally allocated to the Jewish state, the Lebanese occupied a tiny area at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosh_HaNikra,_Israel" title="Rosh HaNikra, Israel">
       Rosh Hanikra
      </a>
      , and the Egyptians retained the Gaza strip and still had some forces surrounded inside Israeli territory. Jordanian forces remained in
      <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian occupation of the West Bank">
       occupation of the West Bank
      </a>
      , where the British had stationed them before the war. Jordan annexed the areas it occupied while Egypt kept
      <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">
       Gaza as an occupied zone
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the ceasefire declaration, Britain released over 2,000 Jewish detainees it was still holding in Cyprus and recognized the state of Israel. On 11 May 1949, Israel was admitted as a member of the United Nations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Out of an Israeli population of 650,000, some 6,000 men and women were killed in the fighting, including 4,000 soldiers in the IDF. According to United Nations figures, 726,000 Palestinians
      <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus" title="1948 Palestinian exodus">
       had fled or were evicted
      </a>
      by the Israelis between 1947 and 1949.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Except in Jordan, the Palestinian refugees were settled in large refugee camps in poor, overcrowded conditions. In December 1949, the UN (in response to a British proposal) established an agency (
      <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">
       UNRWA
      </a>
      ) to provide aid to the Palestinian refugees. It became the largest single UN agency and is the only UN agency that serves a single people.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1948.E2.80.931954:_Ben-Gurion_I">
       19481954: Ben-Gurion I
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 19481954: Ben-Gurion I">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Austerity_in_Israel" title="Austerity in Israel">
       Austerity in Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Provisional_government_of_Israel" title="Provisional government of Israel">
       Provisional
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/First_government_of_Israel" title="First government of Israel">
       First
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Second_government_of_Israel" title="Second government of Israel">
       Second
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Third_government_of_Israel" title="Third government of Israel">
       Third
      </a>
      ,and
      <a href="/wiki/Fourth_government_of_Israel" title="Fourth government of Israel">
       Fourth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      A 120-seat parliament, the
      <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">
       Knesset
      </a>
      , met first in
      <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
       Tel Aviv
      </a>
      then moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
       Jerusalem
      </a>
      after the 1949 ceasefire. In January 1949, Israel held its
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1949" title="Israeli legislative election, 1949">
       first elections
      </a>
      . The Socialist-Zionist parties
      <a href="/wiki/Mapai" title="Mapai">
       Mapai
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mapam" title="Mapam">
       Mapam
      </a>
      won the most seats (46 and 19 respectively), but not an outright majority. Mapai's leader,
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      , was appointed
      <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Israel" title="Prime Minister of Israel">
       Prime Minister
      </a>
      . The Knesset elected
      <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Weizmann" title="Chaim Weizmann">
       Chaim Weizmann
      </a>
      as the first (largely ceremonial)
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_Israel" title="President of Israel">
       President of Israel
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebrew" title="Hebrew">
       Hebrew
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
       Arabic
      </a>
      were made the official languages of the new state. All governments have been
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalitions" title="Coalitions">
       coalitions
      </a>
      no party has ever won a majority in the Knesset. From 1948 until 1977 all governments were led by
      <a href="/wiki/Mapai" title="Mapai">
       Mapai
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Alignment_(political_party)" title="Alignment (political party)">
       Alignment
      </a>
      , predecessors of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_Party_(Israel)" title="Labor Party (Israel)">
       Labour Party
      </a>
      . In those years
      <a href="/wiki/Labor_Zionism" title="Labor Zionism">
       Labour Zionists
      </a>
      , initially led by
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">
       David Ben-Gurion
      </a>
      , dominated Israeli politics and the economy was run on primarily
      <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">
       socialist lines
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Within three years (1948 to 1951), immigration doubled the Jewish population of Israel and left an indelible imprint on Israeli society.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Overall, 700,000 Jews settled in Israel during this period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some 300,000 arrived from Asian and North African nations as part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries" title="Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries">
       Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sachar_pp395-403_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sachar_pp395-403-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among them, the largest group (over 100,000) was from Iraq. The rest of the immigrants were from Europe, including more than 270,000 who came from Eastern Europe,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      mainly Romania and Poland (over 100,000 each). Nearly all the Jewish immigrants could be described as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">
       refugees
      </a>
      , however only 136,000 who immigrated to Israel from Central Europe, had international certification because they belonged to the 250,000 Jews registered by the allies as displaced after World War II and living in
      <a href="/wiki/Displaced_persons_camp" title="Displaced persons camp">
       Displaced persons camps
      </a>
      in Germany, Austria and Italy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1950 the Knesset passed the
      <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Return" title="Law of Return">
       Law of Return
      </a>
      , which granted to all Jews and those of Jewish ancestry, and their spouses, the right to settle in Israel and gain citizenship. That year, 50,000 Yemenite Jews (99%) were
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Magic_Carpet_(Yemen)" title="Operation Magic Carpet (Yemen)">
       secretly flown
      </a>
      to Israel. In 1951 Iraqi Jews were granted temporary permission to leave the country and 120,000 (over 90%) opted
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Ezra_and_Nehemiah" title="Operation Ezra and Nehemiah">
       to move to Israel
      </a>
      . Jews also fled from Lebanon, Syria and Egypt. By the late sixties, about 500,000 Jews had left Algeria, Morocco and Tunisia. Over the course of twenty years, some 850,000 Jews from Arab countries (99%) relocated to Israel (680,000), France and the Americas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The land and property left behind by the Jews (much of it in Arab city centres) is still a matter of some dispute. Today there are about 9,000 Jews living in Arab states, of whom 75% live in Morocco and 15% in Tunisia.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Begin_at_Mass.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Begin_at_Mass.jpg/220px-Begin_at_Mass.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Begin_at_Mass.jpg/330px-Begin_at_Mass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Begin_at_Mass.jpg/440px-Begin_at_Mass.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Begin_at_Mass.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
         Menachem Begin
        </a>
        addressing a mass demonstration in Tel Aviv against
        <a href="/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_West_Germany" title="Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany">
         negotiations with Germany
        </a>
        in 1952. The sign reads: "Our honor shall not be sold for money; Our blood shall not be atoned by goods. We shall wipe out the disgrace!"
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Between 1948 and 1958, the population of Israel rose from 800,000 to two million. During this period, food, clothes and furniture had to be rationed in what became known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Austerity_in_Israel" title="Austerity in Israel">
       Austerity Period
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Tkufat haTsena
      </i>
      ). Immigrants were mostly refugees with no money or possessions and many were housed in temporary camps known as
      <a href="/wiki/Ma%27abarot" title="Ma'abarot">
       ma'abarot
      </a>
      . By 1952, over 200,000 immigrants were living in tents or prefabricated shacks built by the government. Israel received financial aid from private donations from
      <a href="/wiki/American_Jewish_Joint_Distribution_Committee" title="American Jewish Joint Distribution Committee">
       outside the country
      </a>
      (mainly the United States).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The pressure on the new state's finances led Ben-Gurion to sign a
      <a href="/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_West_Germany" title="Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany">
       reparations agreement
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">
       West Germany
      </a>
      . During the Knesset debate some 5,000 demonstrators gathered and riot police had to cordon the building.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Israel received several billion marks and in return agreed to open diplomatic relations with Germany.
     </p>
     <p>
      At the end of 1953, Ben-Gurion retired to
      <a href="/wiki/Kibbutz" title="Kibbutz">
       Kibbutz
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Sde_Boker" title="Sde Boker">
       Sde Boker
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">
       Negev
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1949, education was made free and compulsory for all citizens until the age of 14. The state now funded the party-affiliated Zionist education system and a new body created by the Haredi
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agudat_Israel" title="Agudat Israel">
       Agudat Israel
      </a>
      party. A separate body was created to provide education for the remaining Palestinian-Arab population. The major political parties now competed for immigrants to join their education systems. The government banned the existing educational bodies from the transit camps and tried to mandate a unitary secular socialist education
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      under the control of "camp managers" who also had to provide work, food and housing for the immigrants. There were attempts to force orthodox Yemenite children to adopt a secular life style by teachers, including many instances of Yemenite children having their
      <a href="/wiki/Payot" title="Payot">
       side-curls
      </a>
      cut by teachers. This led to the first Israeli public inquiry (the Fromkin Inquiry),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the collapse of the coalition, and an
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1951" title="Israeli legislative election, 1951">
       election
      </a>
      in 1951, with little change in the results. In 1953 the party-affiliated education system was scrapped and replaced by a secular state education system and a state-run Modern Orthodox system. Agudat Israel were allowed to maintain their existing school system.
     </p>
     <p>
      In its early years Israel sought to maintain a non-aligned position between the super-powers. However, in 1952, an antisemitic public trial was staged in Moscow in which a group of Jewish doctors were accused of trying to poison Stalin (the
      <a href="/wiki/Doctors%27_plot" title="Doctors' plot">
       Doctors' plot
      </a>
      ), followed by a similar trial in Czechoslovakia (
      <a href="/wiki/Sl%C3%A1nsk%C3%BD_trial" title="Slnsk trial">
       Slnsk trial
      </a>
      ). This, and the failure of Israel to be included in the
      <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">
       Bandung Conference
      </a>
      (of
      <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">
       non-aligned states
      </a>
      ), effectively ended Israel's pursuit of non-alignment. On 19 May 1950, Egypt announced that the
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Suez Canal
      </a>
      was closed to Israeli ships and commerce. In 1952 a
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952" title="Egyptian Revolution of 1952">
       military coup
      </a>
      in Egypt brought
      <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">
       Abdel Nasser
      </a>
      to power. The United States pursued close relations with the new Arab states, particularly the Nasser-led Egyptian
      <a href="/wiki/Free_Officers_Movement_(Egypt)" title="Free Officers Movement (Egypt)">
       Free Officers Movement
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_Saud_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Ibn Saud of Saudi Arabia">
       Ibn Saud of Saudi Arabia
      </a>
      . Israel's solution to diplomatic isolation was to establish good relations with newly independent states in
      <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
       Africa
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and with France, which was engaged in the
      <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">
       Algerian War
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1954.E2.80.931955:_Sharett">
       19541955: Sharett
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 19541955: Sharett">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Lavon_Affair" title="Lavon Affair">
       Lavon Affair
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Reprisal_operations" title="Reprisal operations">
       Reprisal operations
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Fifth_government_of_Israel" title="Fifth government of Israel">
       Fifth
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sixth_government_of_Israel" title="Sixth government of Israel">
       Sixth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1955" title="Israeli legislative election, 1955">
       January 1955 elections
      </a>
      Mapai won 40 seats and the Labour Party 10,
      <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Sharett" title="Moshe Sharett">
       Moshe Sharett
      </a>
      became prime minister of Israel at the head of a left-wing coalition. Between 1953 and 1956, there were intermittent clashes along all of Israel's borders as Arab
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_attacks_against_Israeli_civilians_before_1967" title="List of attacks against Israeli civilians before 1967">
       terrorism
      </a>
      and breaches of the ceasefire resulted in Israeli
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retribution_operations" title="Retribution operations">
       counter-raids
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_fedayeen" title="Palestinian fedayeen">
       Palestinian fedayeen
      </a>
      attacks, often organized and sponsored by the Egyptians, were made from
      <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">
       (Egyptian occupied) Gaza
      </a>
      . Fedayeen attacks led to a growing cycle of violence as Israel launched
      <a href="/wiki/Unit_101" title="Unit 101">
       reprisal attacks
      </a>
      against Gaza.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1954 the
      <a href="/wiki/Uzi" title="Uzi">
       Uzi
      </a>
      submachine gun first entered use by the Israel Defense Forces. In 1955 the Egyptian government began recruiting former Nazi rocket scientists for a missile program.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Archaeologist and General
      <a href="/wiki/Yigael_Yadin" title="Yigael Yadin">
       Yigael Yadin
      </a>
      purchased the
      <a href="/wiki/Dead_Sea_Scrolls" title="Dead Sea Scrolls">
       Dead Sea Scrolls
      </a>
      on behalf of the State of Israel. The entire first batch to be discovered were now owned by Israel and housed in the
      <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_Book" title="Shrine of the Book">
       Shrine of the Book
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Museum" title="Israel Museum">
       Israel Museum
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Sharett's government was brought down by the
      <a href="/wiki/Lavon_Affair" title="Lavon Affair">
       Lavon Affair
      </a>
      , a crude plan to disrupt U.S.Egyptian relations, involving Israeli agents planting bombs at American sites in Egypt.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The plan failed when eleven agents were arrested. Defense Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Pinhas_Lavon" title="Pinhas Lavon">
       Lavon
      </a>
      was blamed despite his denial of responsibility. The Lavon affair led to Sharett's resignation and Ben-Gurion returned to the post of prime minister.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1955.E2.80.931963:_Ben-Gurion_II">
       19551963: Ben-Gurion II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 19551963: Ben-Gurion II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">
       Suez Crisis
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Seventh_government_of_Israel" title="Seventh government of Israel">
       Seventh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eighth_government_of_Israel" title="Eighth government of Israel">
       Eighth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ninth_government_of_Israel" title="Ninth government of Israel">
       Ninth
      </a>
      ,and
      <a href="/wiki/Tenth_government_of_Israel" title="Tenth government of Israel">
       Tenth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1956, the increasingly pro-Soviet President Nasser of Egypt, announced the nationalization of the (French and British owned)
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Suez Canal
      </a>
      , which was Egypt's main source of foreign currency. Egypt also blockaded the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aqaba" title="Gulf of Aqaba">
       Gulf of Aqaba
      </a>
      preventing Israeli access to the
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
       Red Sea
      </a>
      . Israel made a
      <a href="/wiki/Protocol_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Protocol of Svres">
       secret agreement
      </a>
      with the French at Svres to coordinate military operations against Egypt. Britain and France had already begun secret preparations for military action. It has been alleged that the French also agreed to build a
      <a href="/wiki/Negev_Nuclear_Research_Center" title="Negev Nuclear Research Center">
       nuclear plant
      </a>
      for the Israelis and that by 1968 this was able to produce
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel" title="Nuclear weapons and Israel">
       nuclear weapons
      </a>
      . Britain and France arranged for Israel to give them a pretext for seizing the Suez Canal. Israel was to attack Egypt, and Britain and France would then call on both sides to withdraw. When, as expected, the Egyptians refused, Anglo-French forces would invade to take control of the Canal.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="position:relative;display:block;width:400px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" style="width:400px;height:300px" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv/400px--Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" class="kskin" data-durationhint="591.05772439106" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" transcodekey="360p.webm" data-title="Web streamable WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-width="400" data-height="300" data-bandwidth="564360" data-framerate="29.97" /&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora, vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file, 400  300 (592 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="400" data-height="300" data-bandwidth="592267" data-framerate="29.97" /&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv.160p.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora, vorbis&quot;" transcodekey="160p.ogv" data-title="Low bandwidth Ogg video (160P)" data-shorttitle="Ogg 160P" data-width="214" data-height="160" data-bandwidth="197184" data-framerate="15" /&gt;Sorry, your browser either has JavaScript disabled or does not have any supported player.&lt;br /&gt;

        <img alt="File:Egypt-Israel Disturbances.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv/220px-seek%3D147-Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:165px"/>
        <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv" target="new" title="Play media">
         <span class="play-btn-large">
          <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">
           Play media
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Egypt-Israel_Disturbances.ogv" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        U.S. newsreel on the Sinai and Gaza invasions
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Israeli forces, commanded by General
      <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan" title="Moshe Dayan">
       Moshe Dayan
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Kadesh" title="Operation Kadesh">
       attacked
      </a>
      Egypt on 29 October 1956. On 30 October Britain and France made their pre-arranged call for both sides to stop fighting and withdraw from the Canal area, and for them to be allowed to take up positions at key points on the Canal. Egypt refused and the allies commenced air strikes on 31 October aimed at neutralizing the Egyptian air force. By 5 November the Israelis had overrun the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinai" title="Sinai">
       Sinai
      </a>
      . The Anglo-French invasion began that day. There was uproar in the UN, with the United States and USSR for once in agreement in denouncing the actions of Israel, Britain and France. A demand for a ceasefire was reluctantly accepted on 7 November.
     </p>
     <p>
      At Egypt's request, the UN sent an
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force" title="United Nations Emergency Force">
       Emergency Force
      </a>
      (UNEF), consisting of 6,000 peacekeeping troops from 10 nations to supervise the ceasefire. This was the first ever UN peacekeeping operation. From 15 November the UN troops marked out a zone across the Sinai to separate the Israeli and Egyptian forces. Upon receiving U.S. guarantees of Israeli access to the Suez Canal, freedom of access out of the Gulf of Aqaba and Egyptian action to stop Palestinian raids from Gaza, the Israelis withdrew to the Negev.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In practice the Suez Canal remained closed to Israeli shipping. The conflict marked the end of West-European dominance in the Middle East.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nasser emerged as the victor in the conflict, having won the political battle, however the Israeli military learnt that it did not need British or French support in order to conquer Sinai and that it could conquer the Sinai peninsula in a few days. The Israeli political leadership learnt that Israel had a limited time frame within which to operate militarily after which international political pressure would restrict Israel's freedom of action.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1956, two
      <a href="/wiki/Modern_Orthodox_Judaism" title="Modern Orthodox Judaism">
       modern-orthodox
      </a>
      (and
      <a href="/wiki/Religious_Zionism" title="Religious Zionism">
       religious-zionist
      </a>
      ) parties,
      <a href="/wiki/Mizrachi_(political_party)" title="Mizrachi (political party)">
       Mizrachi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_HaMizrachi" title="Hapoel HaMizrachi">
       Hapoel HaMizrachi
      </a>
      , joined to form the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Religious_Party" title="National Religious Party">
       National Religious Party
      </a>
      . The party was a component of every Israeli coalition until 1992, usually running the Ministry of Education. Mapai was once again victorious in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1959" title="Israeli legislative election, 1959">
       1959 elections
      </a>
      , increasing its number of seats to 47, Labour had 7. Ben-Gurion remained Prime Minister.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1959, there were renewed skirmishes along Israel's borders that continued throughout the early 1960s. The Arab League continued to maintain an
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League_boycott_of_Israel" title="Arab League boycott of Israel">
       economic boycott
      </a>
      and there was a dispute over water rights in the River Jordan basin. With Soviet backing, the Arab states, particularly Egypt, were continuing to build up their forces. Israel's main military
      <a href="/wiki/France%E2%80%93Israel_relations" title="FranceIsrael relations">
       hardware supplier was France
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rudolph_Kastner" title="Rudolph Kastner">
       Rudolph Kastner
      </a>
      , a minor political functionary, was accused of collaborating with the Nazis and sued his accuser. Kastner lost the trial and was assassinated two years later. In 1958 the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel" title="Supreme Court of Israel">
       Supreme Court
      </a>
      exonerated him. In May 1960
      <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">
       Adolf Eichmann
      </a>
      , one of the chief administrators of the Nazi Holocaust, was located in Argentina by the
      <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">
       Mossad
      </a>
      , which later kidnapped him to Israel. In 1961 he was put on trial, and after several months found guilty and sentenced to death. He was hanged in 1962 and is the only person ever sentenced to death by an Israeli court. Testimonies by Holocaust survivors at the trial and the extensive publicity that surrounded it has led the trial to be considered a turning point in public awareness of the Holocaust.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1961 a
      <a href="/wiki/Herut" title="Herut">
       Herut
      </a>
      no-confidence motion over the Lavon affair led to Ben-Gurion's resignation. Ben-Gurion declared that he would only accept office if Lavon was fired from the position of the head of
      <a href="/wiki/Histadrut" title="Histadrut">
       Histadrut
      </a>
      , Israel's labour union organization. His demands were accepted and Mapai won the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1961" title="Israeli legislative election, 1961">
       1961 election
      </a>
      (42 seats keeping Ben-Gurion as PM) with a slight reduction in its share of the seats. Menachem Begin's Herut party and the
      <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Israel)" title="Liberal Party (Israel)">
       Liberals
      </a>
      came next with 17 seats each. In 1962 the
      <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">
       Mossad
      </a>
      began assassinating German rocket scientists working in Egypt after one of them reported the missile program was designed to carry chemical warheads. This action was condemned by Ben-Gurion and led to the Mossad director,
      <a href="/wiki/Isser_Harel" title="Isser Harel">
       Isser Harel
      </a>
      , resignation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1963 Ben-Gurion quit again over the Lavon scandal. His attempts to make his party
      <a href="/wiki/Mapai" title="Mapai">
       Mapai
      </a>
      support him over the issue failed.
      <a href="/wiki/Levi_Eshkol" title="Levi Eshkol">
       Levi Eshkol
      </a>
      became leader of Mapai and the new prime minister.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1963.E2.80.931969:_Eshkol">
       19631969: Eshkol
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 19631969: Eshkol">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">
       Six-Day War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Eleventh_government_of_Israel" title="Eleventh government of Israel">
       Eleventh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Twelfth_government_of_Israel" title="Twelfth government of Israel">
       Twelfth
      </a>
      ,and
