      <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Thirteenth government of Israel">
       Thirteenth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1963
      <a href="/wiki/Yigael_Yadin" title="Yigael Yadin">
       Yigael Yadin
      </a>
      began excavating
      <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">
       Masada
      </a>
      . In 1964, Egypt, Jordan and Syria developed a unified military command. Israel completed work on a
      <a href="/wiki/National_Water_Carrier_of_Israel" title="National Water Carrier of Israel">
       national water carrier
      </a>
      , a huge engineering project designed to transfer Israel's allocation of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jordan_river" title="Jordan river">
       Jordan river
      </a>
      's waters towards the south of the country in realization of Ben-Gurion's dream of mass Jewish settlement of the
      <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">
       Negev
      </a>
      desert. The Arabs responded by trying to divert the headwaters of the Jordan, leading to growing
      <a href="/wiki/War_over_Water_(Jordan_river)" title="War over Water (Jordan river)">
       conflict
      </a>
      between Israel and Syria.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1964, Israeli Rabbinical authorities accepted that the
      <a href="/wiki/Bene_Israel" title="Bene Israel">
       Bene Israel
      </a>
      of India were indeed Jewish and most of the remaining
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Jews" title="Indian Jews">
       Indian Jews
      </a>
      migrated to Israel. The 2,000-strong Jewish community of
      <a href="/wiki/Cochin_Jews" title="Cochin Jews">
       Cochin
      </a>
      had already migrated in 1954. Ben-Gurion quit Mapai to form the new party
      <a href="/wiki/Rafi_(political_party)" title="Rafi (political party)">
       Rafi
      </a>
      , he was joined by
      <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">
       Shimon Peres
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan" title="Moshe Dayan">
       Moshe Dayan
      </a>
      . Begin's
      <a href="/wiki/Herut" title="Herut">
       Herut
      </a>
      party joined with the Liberals to form
      <a href="/wiki/Gahal" title="Gahal">
       Gahal
      </a>
      . Mapai and Labour united for the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1965" title="Israeli legislative election, 1965">
       1965 elections
      </a>
      , winning 45 seats and maintaining
      <a href="/wiki/Levi_Eshkol" title="Levi Eshkol">
       Levi Eshkol
      </a>
      as Prime Minister. Ben-Gurion's Rafi party received 10 seats, Gahal got 26 seats becoming the second largest party.
     </p>
     <p>
      Until 1966, Israel's principal arms supplier was
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      , however in 1966, following the withdrawal from
      <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
       Algeria
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle#1962.E2.80.9368:_Politics_of_grandeur" title="Charles de Gaulle">
       Charles de Gaulle
      </a>
      announced France would cease supplying Israel with arms (and refused to refund money paid for 50 warplanes).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 5 February 1966, the United States announced that it was taking over the former French and West German obligations, to maintain military "stabilization" in the Middle East. Included in the military hardware would be over 200
      <a href="/wiki/M48_Patton" title="M48 Patton">
       M48 tanks
      </a>
      . In May of that year the U.S. also agreed to provide
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-4_Skyhawk" title="A-4 Skyhawk">
       A-4 Skyhawk
      </a>
      tactical aircraft to Israel. In 1966 security restrictions placed on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab-Israelis" title="Arab-Israelis">
       Arab-Israelis
      </a>
      were eased and efforts made to integrate them into Israeli life.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1966,
      <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Israel" title="Television in Israel">
       Black and white TV
      </a>
      broadcasts began. On 15 May 1967, the first public performance of
      <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Shemer" title="Naomi Shemer">
       Naomi Shemer
      </a>
      's classic song "
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_of_Gold" title="Jerusalem of Gold">
       Jerusalem of Gold
      </a>
      " took place and over the next few weeks it dominated the Israeli airwaves. Two days later Syria, Egypt and Jordan amassed troops along the Israeli borders, and Egypt closed the
      <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Tiran" title="Straits of Tiran">
       Straits of Tiran
      </a>
      to Israeli shipping. Nasser demanded that the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force" title="United Nations Emergency Force">
       UNEF
      </a>
      leave Sinai, threatening escalation to a full war. Egyptian radio broadcasts talked of a coming genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 26 May
      <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">
       Nasser
      </a>
      declared, "
      <i>
       The battle will be a general one and our basic objective will be to destroy Israel
      </i>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mutawi2002p95_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mutawi2002p95-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Israel considered the
      <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Tiran" title="Straits of Tiran">
       Straits of Tiran
      </a>
      closure a
      <a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">
       Casus belli
      </a>
      . Israel responded by calling up its civilian reserves, bringing much of the Israeli economy to a halt. The Israelis set up a national unity coalition, including for the first time
      <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
       Menachem Begin
      </a>
      's party,
      <a href="/wiki/Herut" title="Herut">
       Herut
      </a>
      , in a coalition. During a national radio broadcast, Prime Minister Levi Eshkol stammered, causing widespread fear in Israel. To calm public concern
      <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan" title="Moshe Dayan">
       Moshe Dayan
      </a>
      (Chief of Staff during the Sinai war) was appointed Defence Minister.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Defense_Minister_Moshe_Dayan,_Chief_of_staff_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Gen._Rehavam_Zeevi_(R)_And_Gen._Narkis_in_the_old_city_of_Jerusalem.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2862" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Defense_Minister_Moshe_Dayan%2C_Chief_of_staff_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Gen._Rehavam_Zeevi_%28R%29_And_Gen._Narkis_in_the_old_city_of_Jerusalem.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Defense_Minister_Moshe_Dayan%2C_Chief_of_staff_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Gen._Rehavam_Zeevi_%28R%29_And_Gen._Narkis_in_the_old_city_of_Jerusalem.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Defense_Minister_Moshe_Dayan%2C_Chief_of_staff_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Gen._Rehavam_Zeevi_%28R%29_And_Gen._Narkis_in_the_old_city_of_Jerusalem.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Defense_Minister_Moshe_Dayan,_Chief_of_staff_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Gen._Rehavam_Zeevi_(R)_And_Gen._Narkis_in_the_old_city_of_Jerusalem.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Gen.
        <a href="/wiki/Uzi_Narkiss" title="Uzi Narkiss">
         Uzi Narkiss
        </a>
        , Defense Minister
        <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan" title="Moshe Dayan">
         Moshe Dayan
        </a>
        , Chief of staff
        <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">
         Yitzhak Rabin
        </a>
        and Gen.
        <a href="/wiki/Rehavam_Ze%27evi" title="Rehavam Ze'evi">
         Rehavam Ze'evi
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem)" title="Old City (Jerusalem)">
         Old City of Jerusalem
        </a>
        , 7 June 1967
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On the morning before Dayan was sworn in, 5 June 1967, the Israeli air force launched
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Focus" title="Operation Focus">
       pre-emptive attacks
      </a>
      destroying first the Egyptian air force, and then later the same day destroying the air forces of Jordan and Syria. Israel then
      <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">
       defeated
      </a>
      (almost successively) Egypt, Jordan and Syria. By 11 June the Arab forces were routed and all parties had accepted the cease-fire called for by UN Security Council Resolutions 235 and 236. Israel gained control of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai Peninsula
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
       Gaza Strip
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">
       Golan Heights
      </a>
      , and the formerly Jordanian-controlled
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan_River" title="Jordan River">
       Jordan River
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">
       East Jerusalem
      </a>
      was arguably
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Law" title="Jerusalem Law">
       annexed
      </a>
      by Israel. Residents were given permanent residency status and the option of applying for Israeli citizenship. The annexation was not recognized internationally (the Jordanian annexation of 1948 was also unrecognized).
     </p>
     <p>
      Other areas occupied remained under military rule (Israeli civil law did not apply to them) pending a final settlement. The Golan was also
      <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights_Law" title="Golan Heights Law">
       annexed
      </a>
      in 1981. On 22 November 1967, the Security Council adopted
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 242">
       Resolution 242
      </a>
      , the "land for peace" formula, which called for the establishment of a just and lasting peace based on Israeli withdrawal from territories occupied in 1967 in return for the end of all states of belligerency, respect for the sovereignty of all states in the area, and the right to live in peace within secure, recognized boundaries. The resolution was accepted by both sides, though with different interpretations, and has been the basis of all subsequent peace negotiations. After 1967 the U.S. began supplying Israel with aircraft and the Soviet block (except Romania)
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_and_the_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="Soviet Union and the ArabIsraeli conflict">
       broke off relations
      </a>
      with Israel.
      <a href="/wiki/1968_Polish_political_crisis" title="1968 Polish political crisis">
       Antisemitic purges
      </a>
      led to the final migration of the last
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_Jews" title="Polish Jews">
       Polish Jews
      </a>
      to Israel.
     </p>
     <p>
      For the first time since the end of the British Mandate, Jews could visit the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Jerusalem)" title="Old City (Jerusalem)">
       Old City of Jerusalem
      </a>
      and pray at the
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">
       Western Wall
      </a>
      (the holiest site in modern Judaism), to which they had been denied access by the Jordanians in contravention of the 1949 Armistice agreement. The four-meter-wide public alley beside the Wall was expanded into a massive plaza and worshippers were allowed to sit, or use other furniture, for the first time in centuries. In
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      , Jews gained access to the
      <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs" title="Cave of the Patriarchs">
       Cave of the Patriarchs
      </a>
      (the second most holy site in Judaism) for the first time since the 14th century (previously Jews were only allowed to pray at the entrance).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A third Jewish holy site,
      <a href="/wiki/Rachel%27s_Tomb" title="Rachel's Tomb">
       Rachel's Tomb
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">
       Bethlehem
      </a>
      , also became accessible.
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Egypt" title="Energy in Egypt">
       Sinai oil fields
      </a>
      made Israel self-sufficient in energy.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1968
      <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Levinger" title="Moshe Levinger">
       Moshe Levinger
      </a>
      led a group of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Zionist" title="Religious Zionist">
       Religious Zionists
      </a>
      who created the first
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">
       Jewish settlement
      </a>
      , a town near Hebron called
      <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Arba" title="Kiryat Arba">
       Kiryat Arba
      </a>
      . There were no other religious settlements until after 1974. Ben-Gurion's
      <a href="/wiki/Rafi_(political_party)" title="Rafi (political party)">
       Rafi
      </a>
      party merged with the Labour-Mapai alliance. Ben-Gurion remained outside as an independent. In 1968, compulsory education was extended until the age of 16 for all citizens (it had been 14) and the government embarked on an extensive program of
      <a href="/wiki/Social_integration" title="Social integration">
       integration
      </a>
      in education. In the major cities children from mainly
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardi" title="Sephardi">
       Sephardi
      </a>
      /
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mizrahi" title="Mizrahi">
       Mizrahi
      </a>
      neighbourhoods were
      <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">
       bused
      </a>
      to newly established
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">
       middle schools
      </a>
      in better areas. The system remained in place until after 2000.
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 1968, Israeli forces attacked the Palestinian militia,
      <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">
       Fatah
      </a>
      , at its
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Karameh" title="Battle of Karameh">
       base in the Jordanian town of Karameh
      </a>
      . The attack was in response to land mines placed on Israeli roads. The Israelis retreated after destroying the camp. Despite heavy casualties, Palestinians claimed victory, while Fatah and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PLO" title="PLO">
       PLO
      </a>
      (of which it formed part) became famous across the Arab world. In early 1969, fighting broke out between Egypt and Israel along the Suez Canal. In retaliation for repeated Egyptian shelling of Israeli positions along the Suez Canal, Israeli planes made deep strikes into Egypt in the 19691970 "
      <a href="/wiki/War_of_Attrition" title="War of Attrition">
       War of Attrition
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1969.E2.80.931974:_Meir">
       19691974: Meir
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 19691974: Meir">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/War_of_Attrition" title="War of Attrition">
       War of Attrition
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jarring_Mission" title="Jarring Mission">
       Jarring Mission
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Plan" title="Rogers Plan">
       Rogers Plan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">
       Munich massacre
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
       Yom Kippur War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Fourteenth government of Israel">
       Fourteenth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Fifteenth government of Israel">
       Fifteenth
      </a>
      ,and
      <a href="/wiki/Sixteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Sixteenth government of Israel">
       Sixteenth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In early 1969, Levi Eshkol died in office of a heart attack and
      <a href="/wiki/Golda_Meir" title="Golda Meir">
       Golda Meir
      </a>
      became Prime Minister with the largest percentage of the vote ever won by an Israeli party, winning 56 of the 120 seats after the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1969" title="Israeli legislative election, 1969">
       1969 election
      </a>
      . Meir was the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_first_female_holders_of_political_offices_in_Asia" title="List of the first female holders of political offices in Asia">
       first female prime minister of Israel
      </a>
      and the first woman to have headed a Middle Eastern state in modern times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gahal remained on 26 seats, and was the second largest party.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MV_Netanya.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="483" data-file-width="697" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/MV_Netanya.jpg/220px-MV_Netanya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/MV_Netanya.jpg/330px-MV_Netanya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/MV_Netanya.jpg/440px-MV_Netanya.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MV_Netanya.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        MV
        <i>
         Netanya
        </i>
        , one of the ships assigned to support boats in the
        <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg_Project" title="Cherbourg Project">
         Cherbourg Project
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In December 1969, Israeli naval commandos
      <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg_Project" title="Cherbourg Project">
       took five missile boats
      </a>
      during the night from Cherbourg Harbour in France. Israel had paid for the boats but the French had refused to supply them. In July 1970 the Israelis
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Rimon_20" title="Operation Rimon 20">
       shot down five Soviet fighters
      </a>
      that were aiding the Egyptians in the course of the
      <a href="/wiki/War_of_Attrition" title="War of Attrition">
       War of Attrition
      </a>
      . Following this, the U.S. worked to calm the situation and in August 1970 a cease fire was agreed.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Black_September_in_Jordan" title="Black September in Jordan">
       September 1970
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Hussein" title="King Hussein">
       King Hussein
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Jordan
      </a>
      drove the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">
       Palestine Liberation Organization
      </a>
      out of his country. On September 18, 1970, Syrian tanks invaded Jordan, intending to aid the PLO. At the request of the U.S., Israel moved troops to the border and threatened Syria, causing the Syrians to withdraw. The center of PLO activity then shifted to
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
       Lebanon
      </a>
      , where the 1969
      <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Agreement_(1969)" title="Cairo Agreement (1969)">
       Cairo agreement
      </a>
      gave the Palestinians autonomy within the south of the country. The area controlled by the PLO became known by the international press and locals as "
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_insurgency_in_South_Lebanon" title="Palestinian insurgency in South Lebanon">
       Fatahland
      </a>
      " and contributed to the 19751990
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">
       Lebanese Civil War
      </a>
      . The event also led to
      <a href="/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad" title="Hafez al-Assad">
       Hafez al-Assad
      </a>
      taking power in Syria. Egyptian President Nasser died immediately after and was succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">
       Anwar Sadat
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Increased
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zionology" title="Zionology">
       Soviet antisemitism
      </a>
      and enthusiasm generated by the 1967 victory led to a wave of Soviet Jews applying to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aliyah_from_the_Soviet_Union_in_the_1970s" title="Aliyah from the Soviet Union in the 1970s">
       emigrate
      </a>
      to Israel. Those who left could only take two suitcases. Most Jews were
      <a href="/wiki/Refusenik" title="Refusenik">
       refused exit visas
      </a>
      and persecuted by the authorities. Some were arrested and sent to
      <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">
       Gulag
      </a>
      camps, becoming known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_Zion" title="Prisoners of Zion">
       Prisoners of Zion
      </a>
      . During 1971, violent demonstrations by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Black_Panthers" title="Israeli Black Panthers">
       Israeli Black Panthers
      </a>
      , made the Israeli public aware of resentment among
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mizrahi" title="Mizrahi">
       Mizrahi
      </a>
      Jews at ongoing discrimination and social gaps.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1972 the U.S.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Mafia" title="Jewish Mafia">
       Jewish Mafia
      </a>
      leader,
      <a href="/wiki/Meyer_Lansky" title="Meyer Lansky">
       Meyer Lansky
      </a>
      , who had taken refuge in Israel, was deported to the United States.
     </p>
     <p>
      At the 1972
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_Olympics" title="Munich Olympics">
       Munich Olympics
      </a>
      , eleven members of the Israeli team were taken hostage by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_September_(group)" title="Black September (group)">
       Palestinian terrorists
      </a>
      . A botched German rescue attempt
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_Massacre" title="Munich Massacre">
       led to them all being killed
      </a>
      , along with five of the eight hijackers. The surviving Palestinians were released by the West German authorities eight weeks later without having stood trial, in exchange for the hostages of hijacked
      <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_615" title="Lufthansa Flight 615">
       Lufthansa Flight 615
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haaretz_144-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-haaretz-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Israeli government responded with a
      <a href="/wiki/1972_Israeli_air_raid_in_Syria_and_Lebanon" title="1972 Israeli air raid in Syria and Lebanon">
       bombing
      </a>
      , an
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Wrath_of_God" title="Operation Wrath of God">
       assassination campaign
      </a>
      against the organizers of the massacre and a
      <a href="/wiki/1973_Israeli_raid_on_Lebanon" title="1973 Israeli raid on Lebanon">
       raid on the PLO headquarters in Lebanon
      </a>
      (led by future Prime Minister, Ehud Barak).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1972 the new Egyptian President
      <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">
       Anwar Sadat
      </a>
      expelled the Soviet advisers from Egypt. This and frequent invasion exercises by Egypt and Syria led to Israeli complacency about the threat from these countries. In addition the desire not to be held responsible for initiating conflict and an election campaign highlighting security, led to an Israeli failure to mobilize, despite receiving warnings of an impending attack.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="469" data-file-width="700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg/220px-Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg/330px-Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg/440px-Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israeli_Tanks_Cross_the_Suez_Canal_-_Flickr_-_Israel_Defense_Forces.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        143rd Division crossing the
        <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
         Suez Canal
        </a>
        in the direction of
        <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">
         Cairo
        </a>
        during the
        <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
         Yom Kippur War
        </a>
        , 15 October 1973
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
       Yom Kippur War
      </a>
      (also known as the October War) began on 6 October 1973 (the Jewish
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">
       Day of Atonement
      </a>
      ), the holiest day in the Jewish calendar and a day when adult Jews are required to fast. The Syrian and Egyptian armies launched a well-planned surprise attack against the unprepared Israeli Defense Forces. For the first few days there was a great deal of uncertainty about Israel's capacity to repel the invaders. Both the Soviets and the Americans (at the orders of
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
       Richard Nixon
      </a>
      )
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Nickel_Grass" title="Operation Nickel Grass">
       rushed arms to their allies
      </a>
      . The Syrians were repulsed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Tears" title="Valley of Tears">
       tiny remnant of the Israeli tank force
      </a>
      on the Golan and, although the Egyptians captured a strip of territory in Sinai, Israeli forces
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ismailia" title="Battle of Ismailia">
       crossed the Suez Canal
      </a>
      , trapping the Egyptian Third Army in Sinai and were 100 kilometres from Cairo. The war cost Israel over 2,000 dead, resulted in a heavy arms bill (for both sides) and made Israelis more aware of their vulnerability. It also led to heightened
      <a href="/wiki/DEFCON" title="DEFCON">
       superpower tension
      </a>
      . Following the war, both Israelis and Egyptians showed greater willingness to negotiate. On 18 January 1974, extensive diplomacy by U.S. Secretary of State
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">
       Henry Kissinger
      </a>
      led to a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Disengagement_Observer_Force_Zone" title="United Nations Disengagement Observer Force Zone">
       Disengagement of Forces agreement
      </a>
      with the Egyptian government and on 31 May with the Syrian government.
     </p>
     <p>
      The war led the Saudi government to initiate the
      <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">
       1973 oil crisis
      </a>
      , an oil embargo in conjunction with
      <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
       OPEC
      </a>
      , against countries trading with Israel. Severe shortages led to massive increases in the price of oil, and as a result, many countries broke off relations with Israel or downgraded relations, and Israel was banned from participation in the
      <a href="/wiki/Asian_Games" title="Asian Games">
       Asian Games
      </a>
      and other Asian sporting events.
     </p>
     <p>
      State funding was introduced for elected parties. The new system made parties independent of wealthy donors and gave Knesset members more power over party funding, however it also made them less dependent on existing party structures and able to take their funding elsewhere.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prior to the December 1973 elections, Gahal and a number of right-wing parties united to form the
      <a href="/wiki/Likud" title="Likud">
       Likud
      </a>
      (led by Begin). In the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1973" title="Israeli legislative election, 1973">
       December 1973 elections
      </a>
      , Labour won 51 seats, leaving Golda Meir as Prime Minister. The Likud won 39 seats.
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 1974,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DFLP" title="DFLP">
       Palestinians
      </a>
      attacked a school in
      <a href="/wiki/Ma%27alot_massacre" title="Ma'alot massacre">
       Ma'alot
      </a>
      , holding 102 children hostage. Twenty-two children were killed. In November 1974 the PLO was granted observer status at the UN and
      <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">
       Yasser Arafat
      </a>
      addressed the General Assembly. Later that year the
      <a href="/wiki/Agranat_Commission" title="Agranat Commission">
       Agranat Commission
      </a>
      , appointed to assess responsibility for Israel's lack of preparedness for the war, exonerated the government of responsibility, and held the
      <a href="/wiki/David_Elazar" title="David Elazar">
       Chief of Staff
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Eli_Zeira" title="Eli Zeira">
       head of military intelligence
      </a>
      responsible. Despite the report, public anger at the Government led to
      <a href="/wiki/Golda_Meir" title="Golda Meir">
       Golda Meir
      </a>
      's resignation.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1974.E2.80.931977:_Rabin_I">
       19741977: Rabin I
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 19741977: Rabin I">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Entebbe" title="Operation Entebbe">
       Operation Entebbe
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Seventeenth_government_of_Israel" title="Seventeenth government of Israel">
       Seventeenth government of Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following Meir's resignation,
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">
       Yitzhak Rabin
      </a>
      (Chief of Staff during the Six Day War) became prime minister.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_Orthodox_Jews" title="Modern Orthodox Jews">
       Modern Orthodox Jews
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Zionist" title="Religious Zionist">
       Religious Zionist
      </a>
      followers of the teachings of
      <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Isaac_Kook" title="Abraham Isaac Kook">
       Rabbi Kook
      </a>
      ), formed the
      <a href="/wiki/Gush_Emunim" title="Gush Emunim">
       Gush Emunim
      </a>
      movement, and began an organized drive to settle the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
       Gaza Strip
      </a>
      . In November 1975 the United Nations General Assembly, under the guidance of Austrian Secretary General
      <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">
       Kurt Waldheim
      </a>
      , adopted
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly_Resolution_3379" title="UN General Assembly Resolution 3379">
       Resolution 3379
      </a>
      , which asserted
      <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">
       Zionism
      </a>
      to be a form of racism. The General Assembly rescinded this resolution in December 1991 with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly_Resolution_46/86" title="UN General Assembly Resolution 46/86">
       Resolution 46/86
      </a>
      . In March 1976 there was a massive
      <a href="/wiki/Land_Day#The_protest_of_1976" title="Land Day">
       strike by Israeli-Arabs
      </a>
      in protest at a government plan to expropriate land in the Galilee.
     </p>
     <p>
      In July 1976, an
      <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">
       Air France
      </a>
      plane carrying 260 people was hijacked by
      <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine_%E2%80%93_External_Operations" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine  External Operations">
       Palestinian
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Cells_(RZ)" title="Revolutionary Cells (RZ)">
       German
      </a>
      terrorists and flown to Uganda, then ruled by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Idi_Amin_Dada" title="Idi Amin Dada">
       Idi Amin Dada
      </a>
      . There, the Germans separated the Jewish passengers from the non-Jewish passengers, releasing the non-Jews. The hijackers threatened to kill the remaining, 100-odd Jewish passengers (and the French crew who had refused to leave). Despite the distances involved, Rabin ordered a daring
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Entebbe" title="Operation Entebbe">
       rescue operation
      </a>
      in which the kidnapped Jews were freed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      UN Secretary General Waldheim described the raid as "a serious violation of the national sovereignty of a United Nations member state" (meaning Uganda).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Waldheim was a former Nazi and suspected war criminal, with a record of offending Jewish sensibilities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1976, the ongoing
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">
       Lebanese Civil War
      </a>
      led Israel to allow South Lebanese to
      <a href="/wiki/Good_Fence" title="Good Fence">
       cross the border
      </a>
      and work in Israel. In January 1977, French authorities arrested
      <a href="/wiki/Abu_Daoud" title="Abu Daoud">
       Abu Daoud
      </a>
      , the planner of the Munich massacre, releasing him a few days later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 1977
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatoly_Sharansky" title="Anatoly Sharansky">
       Anatoly Sharansky
      </a>
      , a prominent
      <a href="/wiki/Refusenik" title="Refusenik">
       Refusenik
      </a>
      and spokesman for the
      <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Helsinki_Group" title="Moscow Helsinki Group">
       Moscow Helsinki Group
      </a>
      , was sentenced to 13 years' hard labour.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rabin resigned on April 1977 after it emerged that his
      <a href="/wiki/Leah_Rabin" title="Leah Rabin">
       wife
      </a>
      maintained a dollar account in the United States (illegal at the time), which had been opened while Rabin was Israeli ambassador. The incident became known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Dollar_Account_affair" title="Dollar Account affair">
       Dollar Account affair
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">
       Shimon Peres
      </a>
      informally replaced him as prime minister, leading the
      <a href="/wiki/Alignment_(political_party)" title="Alignment (political party)">
       Alignment
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1977" title="Israeli legislative election, 1977">
       subsequent elections
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1977.E2.80.931983:_Begin">
       19771983: Begin
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: 19771983: Begin">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Camp_David_Accords" title="Camp David Accords">
       Camp David Accords
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/1978_South_Lebanon_conflict" title="1978 South Lebanon conflict">
       1978 South Lebanon conflict
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War" title="1982 Lebanon War">
       1982 Lebanon War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Eighteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Eighteenth government of Israel">
       Eighteenth
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_government_of_Israel" title="Nineteenth government of Israel">
       Nineteenth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In a surprise result, the
      <a href="/wiki/Likud" title="Likud">
       Likud
      </a>
      led by
      <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
       Menachem Begin
      </a>
      won 43 seats in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1977" title="Israeli legislative election, 1977">
       1977 elections
      </a>
      (Labour got 32 seats). This was the first time in Israeli history that the government was not led by the left. A key reason for the victory was anger among
      <a href="/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews" title="Mizrahi Jews">
       Mizrahi Jews
      </a>
      at discrimination, which was to play an important role in Israeli politics for many years. Talented small town Mizrahi social activists, unable to advance in the Labour party, were readily embraced by Begin. Moroccan-born
      <a href="/wiki/David_Levy_(Israeli_politician)" title="David Levy (Israeli politician)">
       David Levy
      </a>
      and Iranian-born
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moshe_Katzav" title="Moshe Katzav">
       Moshe Katzav
      </a>
      were part of a group who won Mizrahi support for Begin. Many Labour voters voted for the
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_for_Change" title="Democratic Movement for Change">
       Democratic Movement for Change
      </a>
      (15 seats) in protest at high-profile corruption cases. The party joined in coalition with Begin and disappeared at the next election.
     </p>
     <p>
      In addition to starting a process of healing the Mizrahi
      <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">
       Ashkenazi
      </a>
      divide, Begin's government included
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agudat_Israel" title="Agudat Israel">
       Ultra-Orthodox Jews
      </a>
      and was instrumental in healing the ZionistUltra-Orthodox rift, however it did so at the cost of expanding the exemption from military service to all
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haredi" title="Haredi">
       Haredi
      </a>
      Jewish students of military age. This led to creation of a huge class of unemployed Haredi Jews (the exemption was conditional on attendance of a religious seminary, so they kept studying until they were too old for military service). By remaining students, they were a massive burden on the state, while also failing to participate in the military burden.
     </p>
     <p>
      Begin's liberalization of the economy led to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyper-inflation" title="Hyper-inflation">
       hyper-inflation
      </a>
      (around 150% inflation) but enabled Israel to begin receiving U.S. financial aid. Begin actively supported
      <a href="/wiki/Gush_Emunim" title="Gush Emunim">
       Gush Emunim
      </a>
      's efforts to settle the
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">
       West Bank
      </a>
      and Jewish settlements in the occupied territories received government support, thus laying the grounds for intense conflict with the Palestinian population of the occupied territories.
     </p>
     <p>
      In November 1977, Egyptian President
      <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">
       Anwar Sadat
      </a>
      broke 30 years of hostility with Israel by visiting Jerusalem at the invitation of Israeli Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
       Menachem Begin
      </a>
      . Sadat's two-day visit included a speech before the
      <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">
       Knesset
      </a>
      and was a turning point in the history of the conflict. The Egyptian leader created a new psychological climate in the
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">
       Middle East
      </a>
      in which peace between Israel and its Arab neighbours seemed possible. Sadat recognized Israel's right to exist and established the basis for direct negotiations between Egypt and Israel. Following Sadat's visit, 350 Yom Kippur War veterans organized the
      <a href="/wiki/Peace_Now" title="Peace Now">
       Peace Now
      </a>
      movement to encourage Israeli governments to make peace with the Arabs.
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 1978, eleven armed Lebanese Palestinians reached Israel in boats and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal_Road_Massacre" title="Coastal Road Massacre">
       hijacked a bus
      </a>
      carrying families on a day outing, killing 38 people, including 13 children. The attackers opposed the EgyptianIsraeli peace process. Three days later, Israeli forces crossed into Lebanon beginning
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Litani" title="Operation Litani">
       Operation Litani
      </a>
      . After passage of
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_425" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 425">
       United Nations Security Council Resolution 425
      </a>
      , calling for Israeli withdrawal and the creation of the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon" title="United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon">
       United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon
      </a>
      (UNIFIL) peace-keeping force, Israel withdrew its troops.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Begin,_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="388" data-file-width="588" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg/220px-Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg/330px-Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg/440px-Begin%2C_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Begin,_Carter_and_Sadat_at_Camp_David_1978.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Begin" title="Menachem Begin">
         Menachem Begin
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">
         Jimmy Carter
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">
         Anwar Sadat
        </a>
        celebrating the signing of the
        <a href="/wiki/Camp_David_Accords" title="Camp David Accords">
         Camp David Accords
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In September 1978, U.S. President
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">
       Jimmy Carter
      </a>
      invited President Sadat and Prime Minister Begin to meet with him at
      <a href="/wiki/Camp_David" title="Camp David">
       Camp David
      </a>
      , and on 11 September they agreed on a
      <a href="/wiki/Camp_David_Accords" title="Camp David Accords">
       framework
      </a>
      for peace between Israel and Egypt, and a comprehensive peace in the Middle East. It set out broad principles to guide negotiations between Israel and the Arab states. It also established guidelines for a West BankGaza transitional regime of full autonomy for the Palestinians residing in these territories, and for a
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_Peace_Treaty" title="EgyptIsrael Peace Treaty">
       peace treaty between Egypt and Israel
      </a>
      . The treaty was signed 26 March 1979 by Begin and Sadat, with President Carter signing as witness. Under the treaty, Israel returned the Sinai peninsula to Egypt in April 1982. The final piece of territory to be repatriated was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taba_(Egypt)" title="Taba (Egypt)">
       Taba
      </a>
      , adjacent to
      <a href="/wiki/Eilat" title="Eilat">
       Eilat
      </a>
      , returned in 1989. The
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
       Arab League
      </a>
      reacted to the peace treaty by suspending Egypt from the organization and moving its headquarters from
      <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">
       Cairo
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">
       Tunis
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Sadat" title="Sadat">
       Sadat
      </a>
      was assassinated in 1981 by
      <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Egyptian Islamic Jihad">
       Islamic fundamentalist
      </a>
      members of the Egyptian army who opposed peace with Israel. Following the agreement Israel and Egypt became the two largest
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_foreign_aid" title="United States foreign aid">
       recipients
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">
       U.S. military and financial aid
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (Iraq and Afghanistan have now
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_cost_of_the_Iraq_War" title="Financial cost of the Iraq War">
       overtaken them
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 1978 the Israeli
      <a href="/wiki/Merkava" title="Merkava">
       Merkava
      </a>
      battle tank entered use with the IDF. In 1979, over 40,000
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iranian_Jews" title="Iranian Jews">
       Iranian Jews
      </a>
      migrated to Israel, escaping the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolution" title="Islamic Revolution">
       Islamic Revolution
      </a>
      there. On 30 June 1981, the Israeli air force
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Opera" title="Operation Opera">
       destroyed the Osirak nuclear reactor
      </a>
      that
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      was building for
      <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">
       Iraq
      </a>
      . Three weeks later, Begin won yet again, in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1981" title="Israeli legislative election, 1981">
       1981 elections
      </a>
      (48 seats Likud, 47 Labour).
      <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">
       Ariel Sharon
      </a>
      was made defence minister. The new government annexed the
      <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">
       Golan Heights
      </a>
      and banned the
      <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">
       national airline
      </a>
      from flying on the Sabbath. By the 1980s a diverse set of
      <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Israel" title="Science and technology in Israel">
       high-tech
      </a>
      industries had
      <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Wadi" title="Silicon Wadi">
       developed
      </a>
      in Israel.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the decades following the 1948 war, Israel's border with
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
       Lebanon
      </a>
      was quiet compared to its borders with other neighbours. But the 1969
      <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Agreement_(1969)" title="Cairo Agreement (1969)">
       Cairo agreement
      </a>
      gave the PLO a free hand to
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_insurgency_in_South_Lebanon" title="Palestinian insurgency in South Lebanon">
       attack
      </a>
      Israel from South Lebanon. The area was governed by the PLO independently of the Lebanese Government and became known as "
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_insurgency_in_South_Lebanon" title="Palestinian insurgency in South Lebanon">
       Fatahland
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">
       Fatah
      </a>
      was the largest faction in the PLO). Palestinian irregulars constantly
      <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">
       shelled
      </a>
      the Israeli north, especially the town of
      <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Shmona" title="Kiryat Shmona">
       Kiryat Shmona
      </a>
      , which was a Likud stronghold inhabited primarily by Jews who had fled the Arab world. Lack of control over Palestinian areas was an important factor in causing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_civil_war" title="Lebanese civil war">
       civil war in Lebanon
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 1982, the attempted assassination of
      <a href="/wiki/Shlomo_Argov" title="Shlomo Argov">
       Shlomo Argov
      </a>
      , the ambassador to Britain, was used as a pretext for an Israeli invasion aiming to drive the PLO out of the southern half of Lebanon. Sharon agreed with
      <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_General_Staff_(Israel)" title="Chief of General Staff (Israel)">
       Chief of Staff
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raphael_Eitan" title="Raphael Eitan">
       Raphael Eitan
      </a>
      to expand the invasion deep into Lebanon even though the cabinet had only authorized a 40 kilometre deep invasion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The invasion became known as the
      <a href="/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War" title="1982 Lebanon War">
       1982 Lebanon War
      </a>
      and the Israeli army occupied
      <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">
       Beirut
      </a>
      , the only time an Arab capital has been occupied by Israel. Some of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Shi'a Islam in Lebanon">
       Shia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Maronites" title="Maronites">
       Christian
      </a>
      population of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Lebanon" title="South Lebanon">
       South Lebanon
      </a>
      welcomed the Israelis, as PLO forces had maltreated them, but Lebanese resentment of Israeli occupation grew over time and the
      <a href="/wiki/Amal_Movement" title="Amal Movement">
       Shia
      </a>
      became gradually
      <a href="/wiki/Musa_al-Sadr" title="Musa al-Sadr">
       radicalized
      </a>
      under Iranian guidance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Constant casualties among Israeli soldiers and Lebanese civilians led to growing opposition to the war in Israel.
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 1982, the PLO withdrew its forces from Lebanon (moving to
      <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
       Tunisia
      </a>
      ). Israel helped engineer the election of a new Lebanese president,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bashir_Gemayel" title="Bashir Gemayel">
       Bashir Gemayel
      </a>
      , who agreed to recognize Israel and sign a peace treaty. Gemayal was assassinated before an agreement could be signed, and one day later
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phalange" title="Phalange">
       Phalangist
      </a>
      Christian forces led by
      <a href="/wiki/Elie_Hobeika" title="Elie Hobeika">
       Elie Hobeika
      </a>
      entered two Palestinian refugee camps and
      <a href="/wiki/Sabra_and_Shatila_massacre" title="Sabra and Shatila massacre">
       massacred
      </a>
      the occupants. The massacres led to the biggest
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-war_protest" title="Anti-war protest">
       demonstration
      </a>
      ever in Israel against the war, with as many as 400,000 people (almost 10% of the population) gathering in Tel Aviv. In 1983, an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kahan_commission" title="Kahan commission">
       Israeli public inquiry
      </a>
      found that Israel's defence minister, Sharon, was indirectly but personally responsible for the massacres.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also recommended that he never again be allowed to hold the post (it did not forbid him from being Prime Minister). In 1983, the
      <a href="/wiki/May_17_Agreement" title="May 17 Agreement">
       May 17 Agreement
      </a>
      was signed between Israel and Lebanon, paving the way for an Israeli withdrawal from Lebanese territory through a few stages. Israel continued to operate against the PLO until its eventual departure in 1985, and kept a small force stationed in Southern Lebanon in support of the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_Army" title="South Lebanon Army">
       South Lebanon Army
      </a>
      until May 2000.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1983.E2.80.931992:_Shamir_I.3B_Peres_I.3B_Shamir_II">
       19831992: Shamir I; Peres I; Shamir II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: 19831992: Shamir I; Peres I; Shamir II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/1983_Israel_bank_stock_crisis" title="1983 Israel bank stock crisis">
       1983 Israel bank stock crisis
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1985%E2%80%932000)" title="South Lebanon conflict (19852000)">
       South Lebanon conflict (19852000)
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/First_Intifada" title="First Intifada">
       First Intifada
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
       Gulf War
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_government_of_Israel" title="Twentieth government of Israel">
       Twentieth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-first_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-first government of Israel">
       Twenty-first
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-second_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-second government of Israel">
       Twenty-second
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-third_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-third government of Israel">
       Twenty-third
      </a>
      ,and
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fourth_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-fourth government of Israel">
       Twenty-fourth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In September 1983, Begin resigned and was succeeded by
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Shamir" title="Yitzhak Shamir">
       Yitzhak Shamir
      </a>
      as prime minister. The
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1984" title="Israeli legislative election, 1984">
       1984 election
      </a>
      was inconclusive, and led to a power sharing agreement between
      <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">
       Shimon Peres
      </a>
      of the Alignment (44 seats) and Shamir of Likud (41 seats). Peres was prime minister from 1984 to 1986 and Shamir from 1986 to 1988. In 1984, continual discrimination against Sephardi Ultra-Orthodox Jews by the Ashkenazi Ultra-Orthodox establishment led political activist
      <a href="/wiki/Aryeh_Deri" title="Aryeh Deri">
       Aryeh Deri
      </a>
      to leave the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agudat_Israel" title="Agudat Israel">
       Agudat Israel
      </a>
      party and join former chief
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rabbi_Ovadia_Yosef" title="Rabbi Ovadia Yosef">
       Rabbi Ovadia Yosef
      </a>
      in forming
      <a href="/wiki/Shas" title="Shas">
       Shas
      </a>
      , a new party aimed at the non-Ashkenazi Ultra-Orthodox vote. The party won 4 seats in the first election it contested and over the next twenty years was the third largest party in the Knesset. Shas established a nationwide network of free Sephardi Orthodox schools. In 1984, during a severe
      <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9385_famine_in_Ethiopia" title="198385 famine in Ethiopia">
       famine
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopia
      </a>
      , 8,000
      <a href="/wiki/Beta_Israel" title="Beta Israel">
       Ethiopian Jews
      </a>
      were
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Moses" title="Operation Moses">
       secretly transported
      </a>
      to Israel. In 1986
      <a href="/wiki/Natan_Sharansky" title="Natan Sharansky">
       Natan Sharansky
      </a>
      , a famous Russian human rights activist and Zionist
      <a href="/wiki/Refusenik" title="Refusenik">
       refusenik
      </a>
      (denied an exit visa), was released from the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">
       Gulag
      </a>
      in return for two Soviet spies.
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 1985, Israel withdrew most of its troops from Lebanon, leaving a residual Israeli force and an Israeli-supported
      <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_Army" title="South Lebanon Army">
       militia
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">
       southern Lebanon
      </a>
      as a "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Security_Zone" title="Israeli Security Zone">
       security zone
      </a>
      " and buffer against attacks on its northern territory. Since then, IDF
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1982%E2%80%932000)" title="South Lebanon conflict (19822000)">
       fought
      </a>
      for many years against the
      <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">
       Shia
      </a>
      organization
      <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">
       Hezbollah
      </a>
      , which became a growing threat to Israel. By July 1985, Israel's
      <a href="/wiki/1983_Israel_bank_stock_crisis" title="1983 Israel bank stock crisis">
       inflation
      </a>
      , buttressed by complex
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Index_linking" title="Index linking">
       index linking
      </a>
      of salaries, had reached 480% per annum and was the highest in the world. Peres introduced
      <a href="/wiki/1985_Israel_Economic_Stabilization_Plan" title="1985 Israel Economic Stabilization Plan">
       emergency control of prices
      </a>
      and cut government expenditure successfully bringing inflation under control. The currency (known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Israeli_shekel" title="Old Israeli shekel">
       old Israeli shekel
      </a>
      ) was replaced and renamed the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_new_shekel" title="Israeli new shekel">
       Israeli new shekel
      </a>
      at a rate of 1,000 old shkalim = 1 new shekel. In October 1985, Israel responded to a Palestinian terrorist attack in Cyprus by
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Wooden_Leg" title="Operation Wooden Leg">
       bombing
      </a>
      the PLO headquarters in Tunis. Growing Israeli settlement and continuing occupation of the West Bank and Gaza Strip, led to the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Intifada" title="First Intifada">
       first Palestinian Intifada
      </a>
      (uprising) in 1987, which lasted until the
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Conference_of_1991" title="Madrid Conference of 1991">
       Madrid Conference of 1991
      </a>
      , despite Israeli attempts to suppress it.
      <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">
       Human rights
      </a>
      abuses by Israeli troops led a group of Israelis to form
      <a href="/wiki/B%27Tselem" title="B'Tselem">
       B'Tselem
      </a>
      , an organization devoted to improving awareness and compliance with human rights requirements in Israel.
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 1987, the Israeli government cancelled the
      <a href="/wiki/IAI_Lavi" title="IAI Lavi">
       IAI Lavi
      </a>
      project, an attempt to develop an independent Israeli fighter aircraft. The Israelis found themselves unable to sustain the huge development costs, and faced U.S. opposition to a project that threatened U.S. influence in Israel and U.S. global military ascendancy. In September 1988, Israel launched an
      <a href="/wiki/Ofeq" title="Ofeq">
       Ofeq
      </a>
      reconsaissance satellite into orbit, using a
      <a href="/wiki/Shavit" title="Shavit">
       Shavit
      </a>
      rocket, thus becoming one of only eight countries possessing a capacity to
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country" title="Timeline of first orbital launches by country">
       independently launch satellites
      </a>
      into space (two more have since developed this ability). The Alignment and Likud remained neck and neck in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1988" title="Israeli legislative election, 1988">
       1988 elections
      </a>
      (39:40 seats). Shamir successfully formed a national unity coalition with
      <a href="/wiki/Alignment_(political_party)" title="Alignment (political party)">
       the Labour Alignment
      </a>
      . In March 1990, Alignment leader
      <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">
       Shimon Peres
      </a>
      engineered a defeat of the government in a non-confidence vote and then tried to form a new government.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_dirty_trick_(Israel)" title="The dirty trick (Israel)">
       He failed
      </a>
      and Shamir became prime minister at the head of a right-wing coalition.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1990, the
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
       Soviet Union
      </a>
      finally permitted free
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aliyah_from_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States_in_the_1990s" title="Aliyah from the Commonwealth of Independent States in the 1990s">
       emigration of Soviet Jews to Israel
      </a>
      . Prior to this, Jews trying to leave the USSR faced
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refusenik_(Soviet_Union)" title="Refusenik (Soviet Union)">
       persecution
      </a>
      ; those who succeeded arrived as refugees. Over the next few years some one million Soviet citizens migrated to Israel. Although there was concern that some of the new immigrants had only a very tenuous connection to Judaism, and many were accompanied by non-Jewish relatives, this massive wave of migration slowly transformed Israel, bringing large numbers of highly educated Soviet Jews and creating a powerful Russian culture in Israel.
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 1990, Iraq invaded
      <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">
       Kuwait
      </a>
      , triggering the
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
       Gulf War
      </a>
      between Iraq and a large allied force, led by the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      . Iraq attacked Israel with 39
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scud_missile" title="Scud missile">
       Scud missiles
      </a>
      . Israel did not retaliate at request of the U.S., fearing that if Israel responded against Iraq, other Arab nations might desert the allied coalition. Israel provided gas masks for both the Palestinian population and Israeli citizens. In May 1991, during a 36-hour period, 15,000
      <a href="/wiki/Beta_Israel" title="Beta Israel">
       Beta Israel
      </a>
      (Ethiopian Jews) were
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Solomon" title="Operation Solomon">
       secretly airlifted
      </a>
      to Israel. The coalition's victory in the Gulf War opened new possibilities for regional peace, and in October 1991 the U.S. President,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">
       George H.W. Bush
      </a>
      , and Soviet Union Premier,
      <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">
       Mikhail Gorbachev
      </a>
      , jointly convened a
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Conference_of_1991" title="Madrid Conference of 1991">
       historic meeting in Madrid
      </a>
      of Israeli, Lebanese, Jordanian, Syrian, and Palestinian leaders. Shamir opposed the idea but agreed in return for loan guarantees to help with absorption of immigrants from the former Soviet Union. His participation in the conference led to the collapse of his (right-wing) coalition.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1992.E2.80.931996:_Rabin_II.3B_Peres_II">
       19921996: Rabin II; Peres II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: 19921996: Rabin II; Peres II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo_I_Accord" title="Oslo I Accord">
       Oslo I Accord
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Assassination of Yitzhak Rabin">
       Assassination of Yitzhak Rabin
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-fifth government of Israel">
       Twenty-fifth
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-sixth_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-sixth government of Israel">
       Twenty-sixth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1992" title="Israeli legislative election, 1992">
       1992 elections
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_Party_(Israel)" title="Labor Party (Israel)">
       Labour Party
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">
       Yitzhak Rabin
      </a>
      , won a significant victory (44 seats) promising to pursue peace while promoting Rabin as a "tough general" and pledging not to deal with the PLO in any way. The pro-peace Zionist party
      <a href="/wiki/Meretz" title="Meretz">
       Meretz
      </a>
      won 12 seats, and the Arab and communist parties a further 5, meaning that parties supporting a peace treaty had a full (albeit small) majority in the Knesset. Later that year, the Israeli electoral system was changed to allow for direct election of the prime minister. It was hoped this would reduce the power of small parties (mainly the religious parties) to extract concessions in return for coalition agreements. The new system had the opposite effect; voters could split their vote for prime minister from their (interest based) party vote, and as a result larger parties won fewer votes and smaller parties becoming more attractive to voters. It thus increased the power of the smaller parties. By the 2006 election the system was abandoned.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton,_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg">
        <img alt="A man in a dark suit on the left shakes the hand of a man in traditional Arab headdress on the right. Another man stands with open arms in the center behind them." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="602" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/220px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/330px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg/440px-Bill_Clinton%2C_Yitzhak_Rabin%2C_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton,_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">
         Yitzhak Rabin
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
         Bill Clinton
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">
         Yasser Arafat
        </a>
        during the
        <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">
         Oslo Accords
        </a>
        signing ceremony at the
        <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
         White House
        </a>
        on 13 September 1993
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 25 July 1993, Israel carried out a week-long
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Accountability" title="Operation Accountability">
       military operation
      </a>
      in Lebanon to attack
      <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">
       Hezbollah
      </a>
      positions. On 13 September 1993, Israel and the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">
       Palestine Liberation Organization
      </a>
      (PLO) signed the
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">
       Oslo Accords
      </a>
      (a Declaration of Principles)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      on the South Lawn of the
      <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
       White House
      </a>
      . The principles established objectives relating to a transfer of authority from Israel to an interim
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">
       Palestinian Authority
      </a>
      , as a prelude to a final treaty establishing a Palestinian state, in exchange for mutual recognition. The DOP established May 1999 as the date by which a permanent status agreement for the West Bank and Gaza Strip would take effect. In February 1994,
      <a href="/wiki/Baruch_Goldstein" title="Baruch Goldstein">
       Baruch Goldstein
      </a>
      , a follower of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kach_and_Kahane_Chai" title="Kach and Kahane Chai">
       Kach
      </a>
      party, killed 29 Palestinians and wounded 125 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs" title="Cave of the Patriarchs">
       Cave of the Patriarchs
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      , which became known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Cave_of_the_Patriarchs_massacre" title="Cave of the Patriarchs massacre">
       Cave of the Patriarchs massacre
      </a>
      . Kach had been barred from participation in the 1992 elections (on the grounds that the movement was racist). It was subsequently made illegal. Israel and the PLO signed the
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Jericho_Agreement" title="GazaJericho Agreement">
       GazaJericho Agreement
      </a>
      in May 1994, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Preparatory_Transfer_of_Powers_and_Responsibilities" title="Agreement on Preparatory Transfer of Powers and Responsibilities">
       Agreement on Preparatory Transfer of Powers and Responsibilities
      </a>
      in August, which began the process of transferring authority from Israel to the Palestinians. On 25 July 1994, Jordan and Israel signed the
      <a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty" title="IsraelJordan peace treaty">
       Washington Declaration
      </a>
      , which formally ended the
      <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">
       state of war
      </a>
      that had existed between them since 1948 and on 26 October the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_Treaty_of_Peace" title="IsraelJordan Treaty of Peace">
       IsraelJordan Treaty of Peace
      </a>
      , witnessed by U.S. President
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
       Bill Clinton
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">
       Yitzhak Rabin
      </a>
      and PLO Chairman
      <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">
       Yasser Arafat
      </a>
      signed the
