      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interim_Agreement_on_the_West_Bank_and_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Interim Agreement on the West Bank and the Gaza Strip">
       IsraeliPalestinian Interim Agreement
      </a>
      on the West Bank and the Gaza Strip on 28 September 1995 in Washington. The agreement was witnessed by President Bill Clinton on behalf of the United States and by Russia, Egypt, Norway and the European Union, and incorporates and supersedes the previous agreements, marking the conclusion of the first stage of negotiations between Israel and the PLO. The agreement allowed the PLO leadership to relocate to the occupied territories and granted autonomy to the Palestinians with talks to follow regarding final status. In return the Palestinians promised to abstain from use of terror and changed the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Covenant" title="Palestinian National Covenant">
       Palestinian National Covenant
      </a>
      , which had called for the expulsion of all Jews who migrated after 1917 and the elimination of Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The agreement was opposed by
      <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">
       Hamas
      </a>
      and other Palestinian factions, which launched
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_suicide_attacks#1990s" title="List of Palestinian suicide attacks">
       suicide bomber attacks
      </a>
      at Israel. Rabin had a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Gaza_Strip_barrier" title="Israeli Gaza Strip barrier">
       barrier
      </a>
      constructed around Gaza to prevent attacks. The growing separation between Israel and the "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Territories" title="Palestinian Territories">
       Palestinian Territories
      </a>
      " led to a labour shortage in Israel, mainly in the construction industry. Israeli firms began importing
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Israel#Foreign_workers" title="Demographics of Israel">
       labourers
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
       Philippines
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">
       Thailand
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
       Romania
      </a>
      ; some of these labourers stayed on without visas. In addition, a growing number of Africans began illegally migrating to Israel. On 4 November 1995, a far-right-wing
      <a href="/wiki/Yigal_Amir" title="Yigal Amir">
       religious Zionist
      </a>
      opponent of the
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">
       Oslo Accords
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Assassination of Yitzhak Rabin">
       assassinated Prime Minister Yitzhak Rabin
      </a>
      . In February 1996 Rabin's successor,
      <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">
       Shimon Peres
      </a>
      , called early elections. In April 1996, Israel launched an
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Grapes_of_Wrath" title="Operation Grapes of Wrath">
       operation
      </a>
      in southern Lebanon as a result of Hezbollah's
      <a href="/wiki/Katyusha_rocket_launcher" title="Katyusha rocket launcher">
       Katyusha
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lebanese_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" title="List of Lebanese rocket attacks on Israel">
       rocket attacks
      </a>
      on Israeli population centers along the border.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1996.E2.80.931999:_Netanyahu_I">
       19961999: Netanyahu I
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: 19961999: Netanyahu I">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-seventh_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-seventh government of Israel">
       Twenty-seventh government of Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The May 1996
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1996" title="Israeli legislative election, 1996">
       elections
      </a>
      were the first featuring
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_prime_ministerial_election,_1996" title="Israeli prime ministerial election, 1996">
       direct election of the prime minister
      </a>
      and resulted in a narrow election victory for
      <a href="/wiki/Likud" title="Likud">
       Likud
      </a>
      leader
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binyamin_Netanyahu" title="Binyamin Netanyahu">
       Binyamin Netanyahu
      </a>
      . A spate of suicide bombings reinforced the Likud position for security.
      <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">
       Hamas
      </a>
      claimed responsibility for most of the bombings. Despite his stated differences with the
      <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">
       Oslo Accords
      </a>
      , Prime Minister Netanyahu continued their implementation, but his prime ministership saw a marked slow-down in the Peace Process. Netanyahu also pledged to gradually reduce U.S. aid to Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 1996, a
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall_Tunnel#Northern_exit" title="Western Wall Tunnel">
       Palestinian riot
      </a>
      broke out against the creation of an exit in the Western Wall tunnel. Over the subsequent few weeks, around 80 people were killed as a result.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In January 1997 Netanyahu signed the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebron_Protocol" title="Hebron Protocol">
       Hebron Protocol
      </a>
      with the Palestinian Authority, resulting in the redeployment of Israeli forces in
      <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">
       Hebron
      </a>
      and the turnover of civilian authority in much of the area to the Palestinian Authority.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932001:_Barak">
       19992001: Barak
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: 19992001: Barak">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit" title="2000 Camp David Summit">
       2000 Camp David Summit
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-eighth_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-eighth government of Israel">
       Twenty-eighth government of Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_1999" title="Israeli legislative election, 1999">
       election
      </a>
      of July 1999,
      <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">
       Ehud Barak
      </a>
      of the Labour Party became Prime Minister. His party was the largest in the Knesset with 26 seats. In September 1999 the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel" title="Supreme Court of Israel">
       Supreme Court of Israel
      </a>
      ruled that the use of torture in interrogation of Palestinian prisoners was illegal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 21 March 2000,
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
       Pope John Paul II
      </a>
      arrived in Israel for a historic visit.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 25 May 2000, Israel unilaterally
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1982%E2%80%932000)#2000:_Israeli_withdrawal" title="South Lebanon conflict (19822000)">
       withdrew
      </a>
      its remaining forces from the "security zone" in southern Lebanon. Several thousand members of the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Lebanon_Army" title="South Lebanon Army">
       South Lebanon Army
      </a>
      (and their families) left with the Israelis. The UN Secretary-General concluded
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      that, as of 16 June 2000, Israel had withdrawn its forces from Lebanon in accordance with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_425" title="UN Security Council Resolution 425">
       UN Security Council Resolution 425
      </a>
      . Lebanon claims that Israel continues to occupy Lebanese territory called "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheba%27a_Farms" title="Sheba'a Farms">
       Sheba'a Farms
      </a>
      " (however this area was governed by Syria until 1967 when Israel took control).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Sheba'a Farms provided
      <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">
       Hezbollah
      </a>
      with a ruse to maintain warfare with Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Lebanese government, in contravention of the UN Security Council resolution, did not assert sovereignty in the area, which came under Hezbollah control. In the Fall of 2000,
      <a href="/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit" title="2000 Camp David Summit">
       talks were held at Camp David
      </a>
      to reach a final agreement on the Israel/Palestine conflict. Ehud Barak offered to meet most of the Palestinian teams requests for territory and
      <a href="/wiki/Concession_(politics)" title="Concession (politics)">
       political concessions
      </a>
      , including Arab parts of east Jerusalem; however, Arafat abandoned the talks without making a counterproposal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In July 2000,
      <a href="/wiki/Aryeh_Deri" title="Aryeh Deri">
       Aryeh Deri
      </a>
      was sentenced to 3 years in prison for bribe taking. Deri is regarded as the mastermind behind the rise of Shas and was a government minister at the age of 24. Political manipulation meant the investigation lasted for years. Deri subsequently sued a Police Officer who alleged that he was linked to the traffic-accident death of a witness, who was run over in New York by a driver who had once been in the employ of an associate of Deri.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 28 September 2000, Israeli opposition leader
      <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">
       Ariel Sharon
      </a>
      visited the Al-Aqsa compound, or
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mount" title="Temple Mount">
       Temple Mount
      </a>
      , the following day the Palestinians launched the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Intifada" title="Al-Aqsa Intifada">
       al-Aqsa Intifada
      </a>
      . David Samuels and Khaled Abu Toameh have stated that the uprising was planned much earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toameh_170-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-toameh-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        170
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlantic_171-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-atlantic-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In October 2000, Palestinians destroyed
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph%27s_Tomb" title="Joseph's Tomb">
       Joseph's Tomb
      </a>
      , a Jewish shrine in
      <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">
       Nablus
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Arrow_(Israeli_missile)" title="Arrow (Israeli missile)">
       Arrow missile
      </a>
      , a missile designed to destroy
      <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">
       ballistic missiles
      </a>
      , including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scud_missile" title="Scud missile">
       Scud missiles
      </a>
      , was first deployed by Israel. In 2001, with the Peace Process increasingly in disarray, Ehud Barak called a
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_prime_ministerial_election,_2001" title="Israeli prime ministerial election, 2001">
       special election for Prime Minister
      </a>
      . Barak hoped a victory would give him renewed authority in negotiations with the Palestinians. Instead opposition leader
      <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">
       Ariel Sharon
      </a>
      was elected PM. After this election, the system of directly electing the Premier was abandoned.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.932006:_Sharon">
       20012006: Sharon
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: 20012006: Sharon">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Intifada" title="Second Intifada">
       Second Intifada
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">
       Israeli West Bank barrier
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">
       Israel's unilateral disengagement plan
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Twenty-ninth_government_of_Israel" title="Twenty-ninth government of Israel">
       Twenty-ninth
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Thirtieth_government_of_Israel" title="Thirtieth government of Israel">
       Thirtieth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westbank_barrier.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="947" data-file-width="500" height="322" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Westbank_barrier.png/170px-Westbank_barrier.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Westbank_barrier.png/255px-Westbank_barrier.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Westbank_barrier.png/340px-Westbank_barrier.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westbank_barrier.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">
         Israeli West Bank barrier
        </a>
        route built (red), under construction (pink) and proposed (white), as of June 2011
        <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The failure of the peace process, increased Palestinian terror and occasional
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%932006_Shebaa_Farms_conflict" title="20002006 Shebaa Farms conflict">
       attacks
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">
       Hezbollah
      </a>
      from Lebanon, led much of the Israeli public and political leadership to lose confidence in the Palestinian Authority as a peace partner. Most felt that many Palestinians viewed the peace treaty with Israel as a temporary measure only.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many Israelis were thus anxious to disengage from the Palestinians. In response to a wave of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_suicide_attacks#2000s" title="List of Palestinian suicide attacks">
       suicide bomb attacks
      </a>
      , culminating in the "
      <a href="/wiki/Passover_massacre" title="Passover massacre">
       Passover massacre
      </a>
      " (see
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Israeli_civilian_casualties_in_the_Second_Intifada" title="List of Israeli civilian casualties in the Second Intifada">
       List of Israeli civilian casualties in the Second Intifada
      </a>
      ), Israel launched
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Defensive_Shield" title="Operation Defensive Shield">
       Operation Defensive Shield
      </a>
      in March 2002, and Sharon began the construction of a
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">
       barrier
      </a>
      around the West Bank. Around the same time, the Israeli town of
      <a href="/wiki/Sderot" title="Sderot">
       Sderot
      </a>
      and other Israeli communities near Gaza became subject to constant
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel" title="Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel">
       shelling
      </a>
      and mortar bomb attacks from Gaza.
     </p>
     <p>
      Thousands of Jews from Latin America began
      <a href="/wiki/Aliyah_from_Latin_America_in_the_2000s" title="Aliyah from Latin America in the 2000s">
       arriving
      </a>
      in Israel due to economic crises in their countries of origin. In January 2003 separate
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_2003" title="Israeli legislative election, 2003">
       elections
      </a>
      were held for the Knesset. Likud won the most seats (27). An anti-religion party,
      <a href="/wiki/Shinui" title="Shinui">
       Shinui
      </a>
      , led by media pundit
      <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lapid" title="Tommy Lapid">
       Tommy Lapid
      </a>
      , won 15 seats on a secularist platform, making it the third largest party (ahead of orthodox
      <a href="/wiki/Shas" title="Shas">
       Shas
      </a>
      ). Internal fighting led to Shinui's demise at the next election. In 2004, the
      <a href="/wiki/African_Hebrew_Israelites_of_Jerusalem" title="African Hebrew Israelites of Jerusalem">
       Black Hebrews
      </a>
      were granted permanent residency in Israel. The group had begun migrating to Israel 25 years earlier from the United States, but had not been recognized as Jews by the state and hence not granted citizenship under Israel's
      <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Return" title="Law of Return">
       Law of Return
      </a>
      . They had settled in Israel without official status. From 2004 onwards, they received citizen's rights.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Sharon government embarked on an extensive program of construction of
      <a href="/wiki/Desalination#Israel" title="Desalination">
       desalinization plants
      </a>
      that freed Israel of the fear of drought. Some of the Israeli desalinization plants are the largest of their kind in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 2004, Israel launched
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Rainbow_(2004)" title="Operation Rainbow (2004)">
       Operation Rainbow
      </a>
      in southern Gaza to create a safer environment for the IDF soldiers along the
      <a href="/wiki/Philadelphi_Route" title="Philadelphi Route">
       Philadelphi Route
      </a>
      . On September 30, 2004, Israel carried out
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Days_of_Penitence" title="Operation Days of Penitence">
       Operation Days of Penitence
      </a>
      in northern Gaza to destroy the launching sites of Palestinian rockets which were used to attack Israeli towns. In 2005, all Jewish settlers were evacuated from
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
       Gaza
      </a>
      (some forcibly) and their homes demolished.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan" title="Israel's unilateral disengagement plan">
       Disengagement from the Gaza Strip
      </a>
      was completed on 12 September 2005. Military disengagement from the northern West Bank was completed ten days later.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005 Sharon left the Likud and formed a new party called
      <a href="/wiki/Kadima" title="Kadima">
       Kadima
      </a>
      , which accepted that the peace process would lead to creation of a Palestinian state. He was joined by many leading figures from both Likud and Labour.
     </p>
     <p>
      Hamas won the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_legislative_election,_2006" title="Palestinian legislative election, 2006">
       Palestinian legislative election, 2006
      </a>
      , the first and only genuinely free Palestinian elections. Hamas' leaders rejected all agreements signed with Israel, refused to recognize Israel's right to exist, refused to abandon terror, and occasionally
      <a href="/wiki/Hamas%E2%80%93UNRWA_Holocaust_dispute" title="HamasUNRWA Holocaust dispute">
       claimed the Holocaust was a Jewish conspiracy
      </a>
      . The withdrawal and Hamas victory left the status of Gaza unclear, Israel claimed it was no longer an occupying power but continued to control air and sea access to Gaza although it did not exercise
      <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
       sovereignty
      </a>
      on the ground. Egypt insisted that it was still occupied and refused to open border crossings with Gaza, although it was free to do so.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On April 2006
      <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">
       Ariel Sharon
      </a>
      was incapacitated by a severe
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haemorrhagic_stroke" title="Haemorrhagic stroke">
       haemorrhagic stroke
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">
       Ehud Olmert
      </a>
      became
      <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Israel" title="Prime Minister of Israel">
       Prime Minister
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.932009:_Olmert">
       20062009: Olmert
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: 20062009: Olmert">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Hamas_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hamas cross-border raid">
       2006 Hamas cross-border raid
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">
       2006 Lebanon War
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008-09)" title="Gaza War (2008-09)">
       Gaza War (2008-09)
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty-first_government_of_Israel" title="Thirty-first government of Israel">
       Thirty-first government of Israel
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Olmert" title="Ehud Olmert">
       Ehud Olmert
      </a>
      was elected Prime Minister after his party,
      <a href="/wiki/Kadima" title="Kadima">
       Kadima
      </a>
      , won the most seats (29) in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_2006" title="Israeli legislative election, 2006">
       Israeli legislative election, 2006
      </a>
      . In 2005
      <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">
       Mahmoud Ahmadinejad
      </a>
      was officially elected president of Iran; since then, Iranian policy towards Israel has grown more
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Iran_proxy_conflict" title="IsraelIran proxy conflict">
       confrontational
      </a>
      . Israeli analysts believe Ahmadinejad has worked to undermine the peace process with arms supplies and aid to Hezbullah in South Lebanon and Hamas in Gaza,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is
      <a href="/wiki/Iran_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iran and weapons of mass destruction">
       developing nuclear weapons
      </a>
      , possibly for use against Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Iranian support for Hezbollah and its nuclear arms program are in contravention of UN Security Council resolutions
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1559" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1559">
       1559
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1747" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1747">
       1747
      </a>
      . Iran also
      <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_to_Review_the_Global_Vision_of_the_Holocaust" title="International Conference to Review the Global Vision of the Holocaust">
       encourages Holocaust denial
      </a>
      . Following the Israeli withdrawal from Lebanon, Hezbollah had mounted periodic attacks on Israel, which did not lead to Israeli retaliation. Similarly, the withdrawal from Gaza led to incessant shelling of towns around the Gaza area with only minimal Israeli response. The failure to react led to criticism from the Israeli right and undermined the government.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 14 March 2006, Israel carried out an
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Bringing_Home_the_Goods" title="Operation Bringing Home the Goods">
       operation
      </a>
      in the Palestinian Authority prison of
      <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
       Jericho
      </a>
      in order to capture
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Sa%27adat" title="Ahmad Sa'adat">
       Ahmad Sa'adat
      </a>
      and several Palestinian Arab prisoners located there who assassinated Israeli politician
      <a href="/wiki/Rehavam_Ze%27evi" title="Rehavam Ze'evi">
       Rehavam Ze'evi
      </a>
      in 2001. The operation was conducted as a result of the expressed intentions of the newly elected Hamas government to release these prisoners. On 25 June 2006, a Hamas force crossed the border from Gaza and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Hamas_cross-border_raid" title="2006 Hamas cross-border raid">
       attacked
      </a>
      a tank, capturing Israeli soldier
      <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">
       Gilad Shalit
      </a>
      , sparking
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2006 IsraelGaza conflict">
       clashes
      </a>
      in Gaza.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="728" data-file-width="784" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/220px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/330px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg/440px-Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Idf_back_from_lebanon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Nahal_Brigade" title="Nahal Brigade">
         Nahal Brigade
        </a>
        soldiers returning after the
        <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">
         2006 Lebanon War
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 12 July, Hezbollah
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zar%27it-Shtula_incident" title="Zar'it-Shtula incident">
       attacked Israel
      </a>
      from Lebanon, shelled Israeli towns and attacked a border patrol, taking two dead or badly wounded Israeli soldiers. These incidents led Israel to initiate the
      <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">
       Second Lebanon War
      </a>
      , which lasted through August 2006. Israeli forces entered some villages in Southern Lebanon, while the air force attacked targets all across the country. Israel only made limited ground gains until the launch of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Changing_Direction_11" title="Operation Changing Direction 11">
       Operation Changing Direction 11
      </a>
      , which lasted for 3 days with disputed results. Shortly before a UN ceasefire came into effect, Israeli troops
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wadi_Saluki" title="Battle of Wadi Saluki">
       captured Wadi Saluki
      </a>
      . The war concluded with Hezbollah evacuating its forces from Southern Lebanon, while the IDF remained until its positions could be handed over to the
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">
       Lebanese Armed Forces
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNIFIL" title="UNIFIL">
       UNIFIL
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2007 education was made compulsory until the age of 18 for all citizens (it had been 16). Refugees from the
      <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">
       genocide in Darfur
      </a>
      , mostly Muslim, arrived in Israel illegally, with some given Asylum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_from_Africa_to_Israel" title="Illegal immigration from Africa to Israel">
       Illegal immigrants
      </a>
      arrived mainly from Africa in addition to foreign workers overstaying their visas. The numbers of such migrants are not known, and estimates vary between 30,000 and over 100,000.
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 2007, Hamas took control of the Gaza Strip in the course of the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">
       Battle of Gaza
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_181-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Guardian-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      seizing government institutions and replacing Fatah and other government officials with its own.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intern_fight_p14-15_182-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-intern_fight_p14-15-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the takeover, Egypt and Israel imposed a partial
      <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">
       blockade
      </a>
      , on the grounds that Fatah had fled and was no longer providing security on the Palestinian side, and to prevent arms smuggling by terrorist groups. On 6 September 2007, the Israeli Air Force
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Orchard" title="Operation Orchard">
       destroyed
      </a>
      a nuclear reactor in Syria. On 28 February 2008, Israel launched a
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Hot_Winter" title="Operation Hot Winter">
       military campaign
      </a>
      in Gaza in response to the constant firing of
      <a href="/wiki/Qassam_rocket" title="Qassam rocket">
       Qassam rockets
      </a>
      by Hamas militants. On July 16, 2008, Hezbollah
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Israel-Hezbollah_prisoner_swap" title="2008 Israel-Hezbollah prisoner swap">
       swapped
      </a>
      the bodies of Israeli soldiers
      <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Goldwasser" title="Ehud Goldwasser">
       Ehud Goldwasser
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Eldad_Regev" title="Eldad Regev">
       Eldad Regev
      </a>
      , kidnapped in 2006, in exchange for the Lebanese terrorist
      <a href="/wiki/Samir_Kuntar" title="Samir Kuntar">
       Samir Kuntar
      </a>
      , four
      <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_prisoners_in_Israel" title="Lebanese prisoners in Israel">
       Hezbollah prisoners
      </a>
      , and the bodies of 199 Palestinian Arab and Lebanese fighters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Olmert came under investigation for corruption and this led him to announce on 30 July 2008, that he would be stepping down as Prime Minister following election of a new leader of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kadima" title="Kadima">
       Kadima
      </a>
      party in September 2008.
      <a href="/wiki/Tzipi_Livni" title="Tzipi Livni">
       Tzipi Livni
      </a>
      won the election, but was unable to form a coalition and Olmert remained in office until the general election. Israel carried out
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Cast_Lead" title="Operation Cast Lead">
       Operation Cast Lead
      </a>
      in the Gaza Strip from 27 December 2008 to 18 January 2009 in response to rocket attacks from Hamas militants,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gw_184-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gw-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      leading to a decrease of
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel,_2009" title="List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel, 2009">
       Palestinian rocket attacks
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shabak_185-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shabak-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        185
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.93present:_Netanyahu_II">
       2009present: Netanyahu II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: 2009present: Netanyahu II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/2011_Israeli_social_justice_protests" title="2011 Israeli social justice protests">
       2011 Israeli social justice protests
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit_prisoner_exchange" title="Gilad Shalit prisoner exchange">
       Gilad Shalit prisoner exchange
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pillar_of_Defense" title="Operation Pillar of Defense">
       Operation Pillar of Defense
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 IsraelGaza conflict">
       2014 IsraelGaza conflict
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty-second_government_of_Israel" title="Thirty-second government of Israel">
       Thirty-second
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty-third_government_of_Israel" title="Thirty-third government of Israel">
       Thirty-third
      </a>
      ,and
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty-fourth_government_of_Israel" title="Thirty-fourth government of Israel">
       Thirty-fourth
      </a>
      governments of Israel
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_2009" title="Israeli legislative election, 2009">
       2009 legislative election
      </a>
      Likud won 27 seats and Kadima 28; however, the right-wing camp won a majority of seats, and President Shimon Peres called on Netanyahu to form the government. Russian immigrant-dominated
      <a href="/wiki/Yisrael_Beiteinu" title="Yisrael Beiteinu">
       Yisrael Beiteinu
      </a>
      came third with 15 seats, and Labour was reduced to fourth place with 13 seats. In 2009, Israeli billionaire
      <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Tshuva" title="Yitzhak Tshuva">
       Yitzhak Tshuva
      </a>
      announced the discovery of
      <a href="/wiki/Tamar_gas_field" title="Tamar gas field">
       huge natural gas reserves
      </a>
      off the coast of Israel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 31 May 2010, an
      <a href="/wiki/Gaza_flotilla_raid" title="Gaza flotilla raid">
       international incident
      </a>
      broke out in the Mediterranean Sea when foreign activists trying to break the
      <a href="/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip#Naval_blockade" title="Blockade of the Gaza Strip">
       maritime blockade
      </a>
      over Gaza, clashed with Israeli troops. During the struggle, nine Turkish activists were killed. In late September 2010 took place
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_negotiations_between_Israel_and_the_Palestinians_(2010-2011)" title="Direct negotiations between Israel and the Palestinians (2010-2011)">
       direct negotiations between Israel and the Palestinians
      </a>
      without success. As a defensive countermeasure to the rocket threat against Israel's civilian population, at the end of March 2011 Israel began to operate the advanced mobile air defence system "
      <a href="/wiki/Iron_Dome" title="Iron Dome">
       Iron Dome
      </a>
      "
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atSpecs_187-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-atSpecs-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        187
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in the southern region of Israel and along the border with the Gaza Strip.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg/220px-Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg/330px-Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg/440px-Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israel_Housing_Protests_Tel_Aviv_August_6_2011b.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/2011_Israeli_social_justice_protests" title="2011 Israeli social justice protests">
         Protest
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
         Tel Aviv
        </a>
        on 6 August 2011
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 14 July 2011, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Israeli_housing_protests" title="2011 Israeli housing protests">
       largest social protest in the history of Israel
      </a>
      began in which hundreds of thousands of protesters from a variety of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socio-economic" title="Socio-economic">
       socio-economic
      </a>
      and religious backgrounds in Israel protested against the continuing rise in the
      <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">
       cost of living
      </a>
      (particularly housing) and the deterioration of public services in the country (such as health and education). The peak of the demonstrations took place on 3 September 2011, in which about 400,000 people demonstrated across the country.
     </p>
     <p>
      In October 2011,
      <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit_prisoner_exchange" title="Gilad Shalit prisoner exchange">
       a deal was reached
      </a>
      between Israel and
      <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">
       Hamas
      </a>
      , by which the kidnapped Israeli soldier
      <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Shalit" title="Gilad Shalit">
       Gilad Shalit
      </a>
      was released in exchange for 1,027
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_prisoners_in_Israel" title="Palestinian prisoners in Israel">
       Palestinians
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel" title="Arab citizens of Israel">
       Arab-Israeli
      </a>
      prisoners.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        188
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated8_189-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated8-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        189
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2012, Secretary-general of the
      <a href="/wiki/Popular_Resistance_Committees" title="Popular Resistance Committees">
       Popular Resistance Committees
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zuhir_al-Qaisi" title="Zuhir al-Qaisi">
       Zuhir al-Qaisi
      </a>
      , a senior PRC member and two additional Palestinian militants were assassinated during a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_targeted_killings" title="Israeli targeted killings">
       targeted killing
      </a>
      carried out by Israeli forces in Gaza.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
       <a href="#cite_note-190">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        190
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        191
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Palestinian armed factions in the Gaza Strip, led by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad" title="Palestinian Islamic Jihad">
       Islamic Jihad
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Popular_Resistance_Committees" title="Popular Resistance Committees">
       Popular Resistance Committees
      </a>
      , fired a massive amount of rockets towards southern Israel in retaliation, sparking five days of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/March_2012_Gaza-Israel_clashes" title="March 2012 Gaza-Israel clashes">
       clashes
      </a>
      along the Gaza border.
     </p>
     <p>
      In May 2012, Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu reached an agreement with the Head of Opposition
      <a href="/wiki/Shaul_Mofaz" title="Shaul Mofaz">
       Shaul Mofaz
      </a>
      for
      <a href="/wiki/Kadima" title="Kadima">
       Kadima
      </a>
      to join the government, thus canceling the early election supposed to be held in September.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_192-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_192-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in July, the Kadima party left Netanyahu's government due to a dispute concerning
      <a href="/wiki/Plesner_Committee" title="Plesner Committee">
       military conscription for ultra-Orthodox Jews in Israel
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        193
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 2012, Israel
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_transfer_of_Palestinian_militant_bodies_(2012)" title="Israeli transfer of Palestinian militant bodies (2012)">
       transferred the bodies of 91 Palestinian suicide bombers and other militants
      </a>
      as part of what Mark Regev, spokesman for Netanyahu, described as a "humanitarian gesture" to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">
       PA
      </a>
      chairman
      <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">
       Mahmoud Abbas
      </a>
      to help revive the peace talks, and reinstate direct negotiations between Israel and the Palestinians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        194
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 21 October 2012, United States and Israel began their biggest joint air and missile defense exercise, known as
      <a href="/wiki/2012_US-Israel_military_exercise" title="2012 US-Israel military exercise">
       Austere Challenge 12
      </a>
      , involving around 3,500 U.S. troops in the region along with 1,000 IDF personnel, expected to last three weeks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
       <a href="#cite_note-195">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        195
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Germany and Britain also participated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
       <a href="#cite_note-196">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        196
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In response to over a hundred rocket attacks on southern Israeli cities, Israel began an
      <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pillar_of_Defense" title="Operation Pillar of Defense">
       operation
      </a>
      in Gaza on 14 November 2012, with the targeted killing of
      <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Jabari" title="Ahmed Jabari">
       Ahmed Jabari
      </a>
      , chief of Hamas military wing, and airstrikes against twenty underground sites housing long-range missile launchers capable of striking Tel Aviv. In January 2013, construction of the
      <a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Egypt_barrier" title="IsraelEgypt barrier">
       barrier
      </a>
      on the Israeli-Egyptian border was completed in its main section.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
       <a href="#cite_note-197">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        197
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Benjamin Netanyahu was elected Prime Minister again after the
      <a href="/wiki/Likud_Yisrael_Beiteinu" title="Likud Yisrael Beiteinu">
       Likud Yisrael Beiteinu
      </a>
      alliance won the most seats (31) in the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_2013" title="Israeli legislative election, 2013">
       2013 legislative election
      </a>
      and formed a coalition government with secular centrist
      <a href="/wiki/Yesh_Atid" title="Yesh Atid">
       Yesh Atid
      </a>
      party (19), rightist
      <a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Home" title="The Jewish Home">
       The Jewish Home
      </a>
      (12) and Livni's
      <a href="/wiki/Hatnuah" title="Hatnuah">
       Hatnuah
      </a>
      (6), excluding Haredi parties. Labour came in third with 15 seats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
       <a href="#cite_note-198">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        198
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In July 2013, as a "good will gesture" to restart
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_Israeli-Palestinian_peace_talks" title="2013 Israeli-Palestinian peace talks">
       peace talks
      </a>
      with the Palestinian Authority, Israel agreed to release 104 Palestinian prisoners, most of whom had been in jail since before the 1993 Oslo Accords,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wash_Post_2013-07-28_199-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wash_Post_2013-07-28-199">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        199
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including militants who had killed Israeli civilians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wash_Post_2013-07-28_199-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wash_Post_2013-07-28-199">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        199
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 2014, Israel suspended peace talks after Hamas and Fatah agreed to form a unity government.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
       <a href="#cite_note-201">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        201
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Following an escalation of rocket attacks by Hamas, Israel started an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Protective_Edge" title="Operation Protective Edge">
       operation
      </a>
      in the Gaza Strip on 8 July 2014,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        202
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which included a ground incursion aimed at destroying the
      <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_tunnel_warfare_in_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Palestinian tunnel warfare in the Gaza Strip">
       cross-border tunnels
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        203
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Differences over the budget and a
      <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_proposal:_Israel_as_the_Nation-State_of_the_Jewish_People" title="Basic Law proposal: Israel as the Nation-State of the Jewish People">
       "Jewish state" bill
      </a>
      triggered early elections in December 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        204
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the
      <a href="/wiki/Israeli_legislative_election,_2015" title="Israeli legislative election, 2015">
       2015 Israeli elections
      </a>
      , Netanyahu renewed his mandate as Prime Minister when
      <a href="/wiki/Likud" title="Likud">
       Likud
      </a>
      obtained 30 seats and formed a right-wing coalition government with
      <a href="/wiki/Kulanu" title="Kulanu">
       Kulanu
      </a>
      (10),
      <a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Home" title="The Jewish Home">
       The Jewish Home
      </a>
      (8), and Orthodox parties
      <a href="/wiki/Shas" title="Shas">
       Shas
      </a>
      (7) and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Torah_Judaism" title="United Torah Judaism">
       United Torah Judaism
      </a>
      (6), the bare minimum of seats required to form a coalition. The
      <a href="/wiki/Zionist_Union" title="Zionist Union">
       Zionist Union
      </a>
      alliance came second with 24 seats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
       <a href="#cite_note-205">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        205
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
